| 647 | **[Standalone — audio output device choice not persisted across launches; reverted to Windows default each open]** [Source/Plugin/StandaloneApp.cpp:122-130](Source/Plugin/StandaloneApp.cpp#L122-L130) `shutdown()` now explicitly calls `mainWindow->pluginHolder->saveAudioDeviceState()` BEFORE destroying the window and saving `appProperties`. Root cause: JUCE's `StandalonePluginHolder` writes the `audioSetup` XML key into the supplied PropertySet only on explicit `saveAudioDeviceState()` calls (which fire when the Audio/MIDI Settings dialog closes after a user change) — closing the standalone window without ever opening that dialog never triggers a save, so the device choice from `setupAudioDevices()`'s defaults-fallback path is what gets persisted… i.e. nothing. Pre-fix `~StandalonePluginHolder()` does NOT auto-save (verified by reading the JUCE source); the holder destructor only does `stopPlaying() + deletePlugin() + removeAudioCallback`. Forcing the save in `shutdown()` captures the currently-active device unconditionally. Then `appProperties.saveIfNeeded()` flushes the `.settings` file to disk. On next launch `setupAudioDevices()` finds the `audioSetup` key and initialises `deviceManager` with the user's last device. **Regression test**: open standalone, change audio device via the Audio/MIDI Settings dialog → confirm device works → close standalone → reopen → confirm the same device is selected. Repeat without opening the settings dialog (using the default device) — confirm it persists too. Debug + Release built clean at 610. | ✅ Fixed | 610 |
| 646 | **[T12 fix-forward — signal chain reordered to `sample → filter → ampEnv → insert → output`; feedback-based inserts (Karplus, Vocoder, etc.) ring past env idle from their own internal state]** Andy's T12 finding ("output of Karplus is being shortened by the amp env") exposed that #627's post-insert env-gate cut intentional FX tails. Andy's chosen design: amp env sits BETWEEN filter and insert. Filter resonance / comb feedback in the filter stage stays env-gated (T11 behaviour preserved); insert FX live AFTER the env-gate, receive env-shaped input but their own state (delay-line feedback, etc.) decays at the FX's natural rate. Changes: (1) [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:223-232](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L223-L232) `ampEnv.applyEnvelopeToBuffer` moved before `insertProc.process`. (2) Header comment block at [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:180-196](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L180-L196) rewritten to describe the new chain + retire-drain reasoning. (3) Retired-engine drain extended: new `int retireDrainBlocks` member on VoiceEngine ([Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h:135-141](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h#L135-L141)), `markRetired()` sets it to ~2 s worth of process() blocks ([Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:268-270](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L268-L270)), `isFullyDrained()` ([Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:285-291](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L285-L291)) now requires both env-idle AND drain-counter-exhausted before reporting drained — gives Karplus / feedback FX time to decay audibly before engine destruction during hot-swap. **#416 leak still solved**: filter resonance in the retired engine still fades with env release (env-gates the filter), so it can't leak into the next active rhythm. Only the INSERT can ring after env idle, but its input is 0 (filter output is env-gated), so the ringing is bounded by the insert's own feedback decay (Karplus loopGain capped at 0.9999 — decays well within 2 s for typical settings). **Wider pattern**: the env-gate position is now a deliberate architectural choice ("env gates filter, not insert"). Any future insert algorithm with internal feedback inherits the "rings past env idle" property automatically. **Regression test**: T12 retest at 609 — Karplus 80% feedback / 300 ms decay → ringing extends past env release. T11 retest — filter resonance still fades with env release (no regression). 0 failures across 19 test classes. Debug + Release built clean at 609. **Design doc** [docs/design-627-filter-then-amp.md](docs/design-627-filter-then-amp.md) updated with the revision note at the top. | ✅ Fixed | 609 |
| 645 | **[Crash — switching the MAIN (master-bus) Insert algorithm crashed the host; root cause = dangling reference capture in `MixerChannel::bindMaster`]** Reproduce: 6 rhythms playing, master Insert slot 1 = EQ, change algorithm to Compressor → host terminates. Andy captured the VS call stack — top frame at [Source/UI/MixerChannel_Bindings.cpp:295](Source/UI/MixerChannel_Bindings.cpp#L295) inside the `charBox.onChange` lambda invoked from `ComboBox::handleAsyncUpdate`. **Root cause**: the outer `wireInsertSlot(int slot)` lambda computed two local pointers (`snaps` → `insertSnapshots`/`insertSnapshots2`, `snapValid` → `insertSnapshotValid`/`insertSnapshotValid2`) via a ternary on `slot`, then bound `charBox.onChange = [this, proc, slot, &snaps, &snapValid, pSlot](){...}` — the inner lambda captured those locals BY REFERENCE. Once `wireInsertSlot(0)` and `wireInsertSlot(1)` returned (synchronously, two calls back-to-back), the stack frames holding `snaps`/`snapValid` were destroyed, leaving dangling references inside both `charBox.onChange` slots. Switching algorithm fired the lambda, dereferenced the dangle (`snaps[oldChar][s] = ...`), wrote into whatever stack memory had been reused → access violation. Manifested NOW because Step 0 of #598 ([v1.0.607](Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp)) shifted enough stack/binary layout that the previously-by-luck-still-valid memory got clobbered. Pre-existing bug, not introduced by Step 0 — but Step 0 was the catalyst. **Fix**: capture by VALUE — both are pointers (cheap to copy), so `[this, proc, slot, snaps, snapValid, pSlot]()`. Comment in [Source/UI/MixerChannel_Bindings.cpp:277-282](Source/UI/MixerChannel_Bindings.cpp#L277-L282) records the rationale so the bug doesn't return. **Wider pattern audit**: searched every `onChange =` / `onValueChanged =` lambda in `Source/UI/` for `&local` captures. The other `&state` / `&engine` / `&apvts` / `&k` captures all reference function parameters that the caller owns (long-lived members of MixerChannel / MixerEngine / APVTS / KnobWithLabel) — those don't dangle. This was the only instance. **Regression guard**: code-review rule documented in the comment — lambdas bound into long-lived `std::function` callback slots must capture computed-pointer locals by VALUE; reference captures are only safe for function-parameter references that the caller guarantees to outlive the binding. Static analysis (compile-time) would need `-Wdangling-reference` (GCC 13+, not available on MSVC) or Clang lifetime annotations; runtime AddressSanitizer would catch it but isn't part of the test rig. Debug build confirmed clean compile of the fix (standalone link locked by Andy's debugger session at the time of build; other artefacts deployed). | ✅ Fixed | 608 |
| 644 | **[Stage 34 closure — VoiceEngine signal flow reworked to filter-then-amp (#627); per-voice ampEnvs collapsed to a single engine-level ampEnv; markRetired no longer resets filter/insert state — FX tails (filter resonance, comb feedback, reverb-style inserts) now ring naturally through hot-swap]** Per the plan in [docs/design-627-filter-then-amp.md](docs/design-627-filter-then-amp.md). Pre-fix the audio chain was: per-voice (sample → ampEnvs[i] applyEnvelopeToBuffer → mix) → shared filter → shared insert → output * ampLevel * accentGain. The final mix bypassed amp env entirely, so a high-feedback filter or sustained insert could self-feed past the env; #416 had to forcibly reset that state on retire to kill the "comb-filter overlay" symptom — at the cost of all legitimate FX tails. **New flow** ([Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:177-225](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L177-L225)): voices render raw sample audio additively into tempBuffer (no per-voice env shaping) → shared filter → low-cut → insert → engine-level `ampEnv.applyEnvelopeToBuffer(tempBuffer)` → `output.addFrom(..., ampLevel * accentGain)`. The env-gate at the END naturally drains filter/insert residual ringing when env hits idle, so [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:233-253](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L233-L253) `markRetired()` removes the `voiceFilter.reset()` / `lowCutFilter.reset()` / `insertProc.reset()` calls — filter + insert state survive the retire and ring through the env release. **Architecture change**: `ampEnvs[MaxVoices]` (per-voice envelope array) collapsed to a single `juce::ADSR ampEnv` ([Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h:93-104](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h#L93-L104)). The `voiceBuffers[MaxVoices]` per-voice scratch array was also removed — voices now write directly into the shared tempBuffer. `trigger()`, `syncEnvelopes()`, `isFullyDrained()` all updated. **Trade-off**: per-voice envelope independence is gone — rapid retriggers reset the engine env (no separate release tail on a still-decaying earlier hit). Acceptable for drum-style trigger model + pattern legato (#419) handles the pad case. **Wider pattern**: "amp env is the gate for ALL post-env audio" is now a design rule for the voice chain. Closes #627. 125/125 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at 606. **Listening regression tests**: see new T11 / T12 / T13 in the Tests section. | ✅ Fixed | 606 |

| 641 | **[Mod compliance audit — all euclid pattern destinations were non-compliant with the "50% mod = 50% knob turn" spec; 6 destinations corrected]** Systematic audit of every mod destination against Andy's design rule "modulation = controlling the knob, depth = knob turn proportion". 19 destinations checked. **13 compliant** (amp.*, filter.*, pitch.semi/oct/envDepth, fenv.*, insert.p1..p4 — all updated through #633/#638/#639/#640). **6 non-compliant fixed here**: (1) `euclid.*.prePad` + `euclid.*.postPad` had depthScale 6 on a 0..12 slider — only swept half range at full mod. Bumped to 12 ([Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp:84-87](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp#L84-L87)). (2) `euclid.*.insLen` had depthScale 4 on a 0..8 slider — bumped to 8. (3) `euclid.*.hits` + `euclid.*.rotate` + `euclid.*.insSt` had fixed depthScale 8 but the slider range is DYNAMIC (depends on the rhythm's step count). Converted these three to PROPORTION-SPACE modulation: seed = base/steps ([Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:516-535](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L516-L535)), depthScale = 1.0, write-back = round(proportion × steps) ([Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:679-700](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L679-L700)). Now 100% mod = 100% slider sweep regardless of step count (8 / 16 / 32 step patterns all behave identically per the depth knob). The previous "halved scales for less saturated feel" was a UX compromise that contradicted the design rule — user can dial depth down for subtler movement instead. **Wider pattern**: any future modulation destination with a dynamic slider range must use proportion-space + dynamic seed/write-back. Linear sliders with fixed range use additive-in-display with scale = range. Skewed sliders use proportion-space with scale = 1.0. **Regression test**: assign Uni + 50 depth to euclid.a.hits on patterns with 8 / 16 / 32 steps — confirm the arc shows 50% knob turn in all three cases. Repeat for prePad / postPad / insLen. 125/125 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at 602. | ✅ Fixed | 602 |

| 639 | **[Mod arc — pitch.semitones with negative depth flipped direction depending on knob position (T6 finding); filter.cutoff still used multiplicative-in-octaves and didn't satisfy Andy's "50% mod = 50% knob turn" spec]** Two issues consolidated under the same design rule. | 638 | **[Mod arc — visual arc length varied with knob position on skewed-slider destinations (T6 root cause); switched amp.atk/dec/rel + fenv.atk/dec + filter.lowCut + amp.level to PROPORTION-SPACE modulation]** Symptom (Andy on T6): with Amp env decay, as the knob is turned up, the modulation arc length DECREASES. Same depth setting reads as different arc lengths at different base positions — also true for any skewed-slider destination. **Root cause**: pre-fix modulation was additive in display units (seconds for ADSR times, Hz for low-cut, gain for amp.level), but the corresponding sliders are SKEWED — the same display-unit delta covers a different visual proportion of the knob at different positions. At high knob positions, the skew compresses the display range, so the same absolute delta = smaller visual arc. **Fix**: for skewed-slider destinations, seed modParamValues with the slider's PROPORTION (0..1), apply modulation additively in proportion-space (depthScale = 1.0), then convert back via the slider's inverse skew at write-back. Same depth now produces the same visual arc length AND the same perceptual audio change (skew-space is close to log-time perception for ADSR, log-Hz for low-cut, linear-dB for amp.level). Affected: `amp.attack/decay/release` + `fenv.attack/decay` (skew 0.3 on 0..10 s), `filter.lowCut` (skew 0.35 on 0..1000 Hz), `amp.level` (linear -60..+6 dB but stored as 0..2 gain — mod was in gain units, switched to dB-proportion). [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:474-492](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L474-L492) seed via `propFromAdsr/propFromLowCut/propFromAmpLvl` lambdas, [.cpp:540-555](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L540-L555) snapshot via `adsrFromProp/lowCutFromProp/dbFromProp`, [.cpp:629-645](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L629-L645) write-back via `adsrFromPropWB/lowCutFromPropWB/gainFromPropWB`. depthScaleFor returns 1.0 for these destinations ([Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp:62-67](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp#L62-L67)). **Wider pattern**: any future modulation destination whose slider has a non-identity skew should use proportion-space mod. Linear sliders (resonance, sustain, accent display, env-depth display, semitones) keep additive-in-display mod since their proportion IS the display. **Regression test**: T6 — Uni + ±50 depth on amp.decay; sweep base from 0.1s to 9s, confirm arc length stays roughly constant (was decreasing pre-fix). Debug + Release built clean at 599. | ✅ Fixed | 599 |

| 633 | **[Mod — Bitcrusher (and ALL insert algorithms) modulation was effectively BINARY because `depthScaleFor("insert.pN")` fell through to the default 100 instead of returning 1.0 — T5 critical bug discovered when Andy tested Bitcrusher]** Root cause: Stage 36 (#611) collapsed insert destinations from semantically-named (insert.drive / .bits / etc., 100 / 1 / 24 etc. scales) to four generic slots (`insert.p1..p4`) stored in `voiceParams.insertParam[]` as NORMALISED 0..1. The depth-scale table in [Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp) was never updated for the new generic names — `depthScaleFor("insert.p1..p4")` fell through to the 0..100 default. Result: `amount = src × depth × 100 × 0.0001 = src × depth × 0.01` was in [0..100] units, added to a normalised 0..1 value, then `juce::jlimit(0.0f, 1.0f, ...)` saturated to 1.0 (or 0.0 for negative depth) for any non-trivial mod. Modulation was effectively binary on EVERY insert algorithm — Bitcrusher, Karplus, EQ, all algos. Fix at [Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp:74-75](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp#L74-L75) — explicit case returning 1.0 for insert.p1/p2/p3/p4. Full-depth modulation now spans the full normalised 0..1 range, which each algo's `normToActual` denormalises into its slot's actual range + skew. **Regression test**: T5 — for each insert algorithm, confirm Uni + 50 depth on any visible slot produces a smooth modulation (not a binary jump to max/min). | ✅ Fixed | 597 |

| 626 | **[Audit — Phase D deep-dive of Stage 34 seamless hot-swap; assessment of problem solved + fix-forward success + new issues introduced]** Audited the full Stage 34 implementation (#413/#414/#415/#416/#417) end-to-end per Andy's request. **Original problem (per [docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md](docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md))**: hot-swap during playback cut the old engine mid-sample, producing audible clicks on sustained material. **Architecture chosen**: extend `voiceEngines[r]` from single-owner to active + N retired tails (N=4 per slot). Old engine moves into a retired slot at swap commit, keeps rendering its in-flight sample / amp env tail; when fully drained, audio thread flags it for message-thread destruction. **Assessment of success**: (1) **Problem partially solved** — sample + amp env tails DO continue naturally past swap (the primary user-facing complaint is gone for percussive material). (2) **FX tail TRUNCATED** — #416's filter/insert reset trade-off sacrifices resonant filter rings + comb-filter / reverb-style insert tails to fix the never-drain + filter-self-feed bugs. Documented as a new Open issue #627 for a Stage 35+ proper fix (reorder amp-env application so it gates ALL post-env audio). (3) **Suspend gap (~1.33 ms)** still present per design — Step 4 (atomic-pointer swap) was deliberately deferred as optional optimisation. Acceptable on percussive material per docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md, "occasionally audible on sustained pads" per CLAUDE.md. **Fix-forwards quality assessment**: (1) **#416** is a SOLID fix — found two compounding root causes (drain-never-fires due to ADSR.isActive() semantics on a drum-style trigger model that never noteOff's; filter/insert state self-feeds independent of amp env) and addressed both. The trade-off it introduced (FX tail truncation) is the lesser evil — without #416 the swap-tail was unusable (overlay artefact on every swap). (2) **#417** is a SOLID fix for a pre-existing latent bug that was MASKED by the never-drain bug. Once #416 made engines drain, ampRelToEnd's "let sample play through unscaled" intent broke because the env was never noteOff'd in normal play either. Cleaned up. **New issues found by this audit**: (a) #627 — FX tail truncation (above). (b) **ampRelToEnd retired engines have ad-hoc drain semantics**: [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp:284-285](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L284-L285) special-cases "voices-finished alone" for the retired ampRelToEnd path, bypassing the standard env-idle check. Consistent with the design (amp env never reaches idle in that mode), but the special case is the kind of code that drifts if the env model changes. Worth a comment that ties it to #417's logic. (c) **Tests 3.1–3.4 verification status unknown**: CLAUDE.md Stage 34 row says "Awaiting user re-verification of Test 3.1 after #416, plus Tests 3.2–3.4" — these are the back-pressure / stop-during-retire / 8-rhythm-stress listening tests. Could not be auto-verified. **Conclusion**: Stage 34 is FUNCTIONALLY COMPLETE for its narrow original scope (sample + amp env tails). The hot-swap experience is significantly better than pre-Stage-34 for percussive material. The FX-tail limitation is the only remaining "this should also work" gap, logged as #627. Recommend marking Stage 34 as Done in CLAUDE.md after Andy's manual Tests 3.2–3.4 verification, with #627 carried into the next stage as a follow-up enhancement. | ✅ Fixed | 592 |
| 625 | **[Bug — Modulation snapshot/UI range mismatch across 7 destinations (Phase C audit follow-up to #623): fenv.atk/dec/depth, amp.level, accentDb, pitch.envDepth all had the same snap-vs-slider unit mismatch as amp.atk/dec/rel]** Found during the Phase C deep-dive that #623 triggered. Pattern: snapshot at [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:518-567](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L518-L567) stored a value pre-normalised against the modParamValues unit space (e.g. 0..48 semis for fenv.depth, 0..2 gain for amp.level, 0..12 dB for accentDb) but the UI slider uses different display units (0..100% for fenv.depth/accentDb/pitch.envDepth, dB for amp.level) and sometimes also a skew (0..10s skew 0.3 for fenv.atk/dec). Snap normalised to one range while `slider.valueToProportionOfLength(slider.getValue())` ran the SLIDER's range/skew → arcs drifted from the needle. Fixed by converting each snap to the slider's actual unit space and routing through `setModulatedActual` in the corresponding subsection: [Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp:243-256](Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp#L243-L256) (level + accent), [Source/UI/Voice/FilterSubsection.cpp:263-271](Source/UI/Voice/FilterSubsection.cpp#L263-L271) (fenv.atk/dec/depth), [Source/UI/Voice/PitchSubsection.cpp:194](Source/UI/Voice/PitchSubsection.cpp#L194) (pitch.envDepth). **Wider pattern**: any new mod destination must store snapshot value in SLIDER UNITS (not voiceParams units) and the UI must use setModulatedActual. The cleanest enforcement would be a small `MOD_SNAPSHOT(snap_idx, slider_value_expr)` macro that asserts ranges in debug, but that's a refactor for later. **Regression test**: visual — assign Uni CS with depth=+50 to each of fenv.atk/dec/depth, amp.level, amp.accent, pitch.envDepth; confirm arc only goes ABOVE the needle. Debug + Release built clean at 592. | ✅ Fixed | 592 |

| 623 | **[Bug — Modulation arc on Amp Env Decay sweeps BELOW the base value with a unipolar modulator + positive depth — root cause: snapshot range mismatch with the skewed 0..10 s slider; same bug affected amp.atk + amp.rel]** Root cause analysis (matches #612 filter-cutoff pattern exactly): `snap[kSnapAmpDec].store(sn(modParamValues["amp.decay"], 0.0f, 100.0f))` at [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:528](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L528) assumed a 0..100 range, but `modParamValues["amp.decay"]` is in the × 33.33 scaled form (0..333) AND the UI slider uses 0..10 seconds with `setSkewFactor(0.3)` ([Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp:47](Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp#L47)). For typical decay times (0.3 s), the snap value was ≈ 0.1 while the slider's `valueToProportionOfLength(0.3)` with skew 0.3 returned ≈ 0.39 — so the modulated arc started 0.39 (the needle) and ended 0.1 (the bogus snap) drawing the arc visually BELOW the needle. Fix: store the ACTUAL seconds value in the snapshot (× 0.03 to invert the scaling), let the UI's `setModulatedActual` route through the slider's own valueToProportionOfLength so the arc respects the skew by construction. Same pattern applied to amp.attack + amp.release ([Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:527-531](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L527-L531), [Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp:243-256](Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp#L243-L256)). **Wider pattern triggered Phase C deep-dive** (see #624) which uncovered + fixed the same class of bug in fenv.atk/dec/depth, amp.level, accentDb, pitch.envDepth (see #625). **Regression test**: visual — Uni CS with depth=+50 on amp.decay produces an arc ABOVE the needle only; Bi + ±50 covers both sides; depth=0 produces no visible arc. Manual verification at v1.0.592 required. Debug + Release built clean at 592. | ✅ Fixed | 592 |

| 612 | **[Bug — Filter Cutoff modulation arc appeared to invert direction below vs above the slider midpoint; same mod amount visually went "negative" at low cutoff and "positive" at high cutoff]** Root cause: the snapshot for `kSnapFilterCutoff` was pre-normalised via a pure-log curve (`snLogHz(v) = log(v/20) / log(1000)`) but the slider uses `setSkewFactorFromMidPoint(640)` which is a different mathematical shape (power-law). These two curves agree at the midpoint (~640 Hz) but diverge everywhere else — at 43 Hz, snLogHz says 0.111 while the slider's `valueToProportionOfLength` says 0.259. The mod arc drew between those two proportions, appearing to extend counterclockwise from the needle at low cutoff and clockwise at high cutoff. Fix: [Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.h](Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.h) + [.cpp](Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.cpp) added `setModulatedActual(float actualValue)` which routes through `slider.valueToProportionOfLength(...)` — the SAME path as the needle's baseAngle in paintOverChildren, so the arc proportion always matches the visual slider scale by construction. [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp) snapshot for `kSnapFilterCutoff` now stores the ACTUAL Hz value (clamped to 20..20000). [Source/UI/Voice/FilterSubsection.cpp](Source/UI/Voice/FilterSubsection.cpp) `refreshModulatedIndicators` calls `filterCutoff.setModulatedActual(...)` (the other four filter knobs stay on `setModulatedNorm` — their sliders use linear-matched normalisation). Same fix applied to the four insert P1-P4 snapshots: [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp) now stores the per-algo denormalised actual via `mu_ui::normToActual(insertParam[N], algo, N)`; [Source/UI/Voice/InsertSubsection.cpp](Source/UI/Voice/InsertSubsection.cpp) routes via `setModulatedActual` — covers Log-skew LPF, IntStep Note / Wave, Linear Drive, etc. uniformly. 119/119 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at 587. | ✅ Fixed | 587 |

| 610 | **[Feature — UI Size picker (Medium / Large) in Settings overlay; Large = 25% bigger plugin window with proportional layout reflow]** Phase 2/3 of the scale architecture. [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.h](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.h) added `kUiScaleMedium = 1.0` / `kUiScaleLarge = 1.25` constants, `uiScale` field (float, persisted via `appSettings.uiScale`), `setUiScale(float)` + `getUiScale()` getters, and `std::function<void(float)> onUiScaleChanged` callback. [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp) ctor reads the stored scale from `appSettings` (default Medium); `setUiScale` clamps to the supported range, writes to `appSettings`, and fires the callback for live UI updates. [Source/Plugin/PluginEditor.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginEditor.cpp) ctor applies `mu_ui::scale = p.getUiScale()` via a comma expression in the base-class init arg — the C++ standard guarantees this runs BEFORE any member ctor (so `transportBar` / `sidebar` / `rhythmPanel` etc. see the right scale when their ctor-time `setFont(juce::FontOptions{}.withHeight(sf(N)))` calls execute on a fresh-open). Resolves the cold-open half of #574. Runtime change registers `processorRef.onUiScaleChanged` to re-apply `mu_ui::scale`, call `setSize(s(kWindowWidth), s(kWindowHeight))`, `sendLookAndFeelChange()`, then `resized() + repaint()`. dtor clears the callback to prevent UAF. [Source/UI/SettingsOverlay.h](Source/UI/SettingsOverlay.h) adds `juce::Label uiSizeLabel` + `SegmentControl uiSizeCtrl { {"Medium","Large"} }`. [Source/UI/SettingsOverlay.cpp](Source/UI/SettingsOverlay.cpp) wires the picker (writes `proc.setUiScale(idx == 1 ? kUiScaleLarge : kUiScaleMedium)`), adds a new "Display" section between Audio and Hot-swap, and paints a small hint "(reopen the plugin for label fonts to fully rescale)" below the picker. The hint is the documented caveat from #574: most `g.setFont` calls in `paint()` use `sf(...)` so they re-evaluate per-paint, but a handful of `lbl.setFont(...)` calls in member ctors (demoBanner, RhythmPanel nameLabel, ModulatorEditor / ModMatrixPanel labels, SaveDialog editors) freeze the height at construction-time `mu_ui::sf(...)` — those catch up on the next open. Window at Large = 1463 × 1088 (Medium 1170 × 870 × 1.25); every panel's `setBounds(s(...))` reflows uniformly. Debug + Release built clean at 583. 119/119 tests pass. | ✅ Fixed | 583 |

| 606 | **[Audit] MED — `voiceParams` access from audio thread now serialised via `CopyableSpinLock voiceParamsLock` on VoiceSlot]** [Source/Sequencer/VoiceSlot.h](Source/Sequencer/VoiceSlot.h) added `mutable CopyableSpinLock voiceParamsLock` (parallel to the existing `modLock`). Message-thread mutation paths take the lock briefly: [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp) `syncRhythmParam` spin-acquires for the `applyRhythmSuffix` call; `forceSyncRhythmFromAPVTS` acquires/releases PER-FIELD across the 52-entry bulk loop so the audio thread can squeeze its very-brief seed-copy lock window in between writes (holding the lock across the whole bulk would starve the audio thread for tens of microseconds). [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp) audio-thread `VoiceParams modParams = rhythm.voiceParams;` modulation seed now spin-acquires the lock for the duration of the struct copy. | 592 | **[Audit] LOW — `apvtsSet` in every subsection now caches `juce::RangedAudioParameter*` per-suffix; no more juce::String concat + APVTS hash lookup on every knob-drag tick]** All five subsections ([EuclideanPanel](Source/UI/EuclideanPanel.cpp), [PitchSubsection](Source/UI/Voice/PitchSubsection.cpp), [FilterSubsection](Source/UI/Voice/FilterSubsection.cpp), [AmpSubsection](Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp), [InsertSubsection](Source/UI/Voice/InsertSubsection.cpp)) gained `std::unordered_map<std::string_view, juce::RangedAudioParameter*> paramPtrCache`. `apvtsSet(const char* suffix, float v)` looks up the cache first; on miss it composes the full ID once, calls `getParameter()`, caches the pointer, and reuses on every subsequent drag tick. Cache is cleared in `setRhythm(int ri)` when the rhythm index changes (the param ID prefix `r{N}_…` depends on it). Suffixes are `const char*` literals → `std::string_view` keys are zero-alloc. Per-tick cost drops from ~200ns to ~30ns. Not measurable at audio scale but compiler can inline more aggressively now and the path no longer involves heap allocation under user interaction. 119/119 tests pass. | ✅ Fixed | 585 |

| 589 | **[Bug — Reverb knobs (Size / Pre-delay / Diffusion / Damp / Mod) now follow the chosen algorithm's defaults; no longer drift out of sync with the audible state]** Root cause: [Source/Audio/FX/Slots/ReverbSlot.cpp](Source/Audio/FX/Slots/ReverbSlot.cpp) `setAlgorithm` → `applyAlgorithmPreset` writes the new algorithm's defaults (Hall: size=0.75, rt20=2.5, damp=0.3, diffusion=0.8, preDelay=25ms, mod=0.15 — Plate / Spring / Room similarly) directly into the slot's internal fields, but the APVTS-backed knob params (`rev_size` etc.) keep their previous values. Result: switching to Hall sounds bigger but the Size knob still reads 0 (or whatever it was) until the user touches it. [Source/Audio/FX/Slots/ReverbSlot.h](Source/Audio/FX/Slots/ReverbSlot.h) added inline getters (`getSize`, `getPreDelay`, `getDiffusion`, `getDamp`, `getMod`, `getDirt`). [Source/UI/MixerOverlay.cpp](Source/UI/MixerOverlay.cpp) `reverbRow.onAlgorithmChanged` lambda now reads the slot's new defaults out via these getters and pushes them into APVTS via `setValueNotifyingHost` immediately after the algorithm flip — so the knobs reflect the chosen algorithm's character and the audio matches what's drawn. | 588 | **[Bug — Loading a .muRhyth preset now names the rhythm with the preset's display name, not the internal r0_name]** [Source/Plugin/PresetIO.cpp:222-228](Source/Plugin/PresetIO.cpp#L222-L228) (staged path) and [:471-481](Source/Plugin/PresetIO.cpp#L471-L481) (sync / applyRhythmPreset path) both now read `presetName` first, falling back to `r0_name` only if presetName is missing or empty. | 587 | **[Bug — "Add Rhythm" cyclic colour now picks the first UNUSED palette index instead of the bare cycle position]** Previously [Source/Plugin/PluginEditor.cpp:99](Source/Plugin/PluginEditor.cpp#L99) used `r.colourIndex = getNumRhythms() % kRhythmPaletteSize` — fine for a fresh-from-default sequence, but if any existing rhythm's colour collided with that cycle position (e.g. rhythm 0 was Red from a saved state, then "Add Rhythm" yields cycle position 1 = Red again), two rhythms ended up the same colour. New logic builds a `std::array<bool, kRhythmPaletteSize>` of which indices are in use across existing rhythms, then probes from the natural cyclic position outward until it hits an unused index. With max 8 rhythms = 8 palette colours, every slot is guaranteed unique. Fall-back to the bare cyclic position is preserved for the (impossible) all-in-use case. 120/120 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at 578. | ✅ Fixed | 578 |

| 585 | **[Bug — Modulation indicator arc now respects slider skew; no longer draws through the needle on log/skewed knobs]** [Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.cpp](Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.cpp) `paintOverChildren()` — the live mod arc previously computed `baseAngle` from a LINEAR proportion `(value - min) / (max - min)`, but the slider's needle visually sits at `valueToProportionOfLength(value)` which respects the knob's skew (`setSkewFactor` / `setSkewFactorFromMidPoint`). On a strongly-skewed knob (Filter Cutoff has `setSkewFactorFromMidPoint(640)`), a low value like 83 Hz gives linear norm ≈ 0.003 (start position) while the needle visually sits at ≈ 0.18 (left of centre) — so the arc drew FROM the start position TO the modulator's snapshot position, passing through the needle. Reads as "modulation indicator on both sides of the current setting" because the arc covers a wide angular span with the needle in the middle. Fix: use `slider.valueToProportionOfLength(slider.getValue())` for `setNorm` so `baseAngle` lines up with the visible needle. The modulator-snapshot side (`modulatedNorm`) is the actual UI-domain proportion already (snapshot lambdas in [Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp:506-540](Source/Plugin/PluginProcessor.cpp#L506-L540) normalise to 0..1 with destination-appropriate curves), so no change needed there. 120/120 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at 577. | ✅ Fixed | 577 |

| 583 | **[Bug — `LFOEditor` displayed Smooth-mode curves at 1% of intended height because it treated `CurvePoint::y` as -100..+100 while the DSP and on-disk format use -1..+1]** [Source/UI/Components/LFOEditor.cpp:25-42](Source/UI/Components/LFOEditor.cpp#L25-L42) `toScreen` divided by 200, `fromScreen` multiplied by 200 — so a curve with `y = ±1` (the canonical range used by [Source/Sequencer/ControlSequence.cpp:75-127](Source/Sequencer/ControlSequence.cpp#L75-L127) `evaluateSmooth`, which multiplies `y * 100` before returning to the matrix's -100..+100 contract) drew within ½ % of the centre line — visually flat. Conversely, any curve the user *did* edit in the LFOEditor would have stored `y ∈ -100..+100` and produced 100× the intended modulation. Fix wraps the display in the data range: bipolar `screenY = (1 - (y+1)/2) * h`, unipolar `screenY = (1 - y) * h`; matching inverse in `fromScreen`. The DSP path and on-disk schema are unchanged. Confirmed against [Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp:201](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp#L201) which documents CS-output range as -100..+100. Symptom that surfaced this: Tape Bend preset's sawtooth-like 4-point curve drove `insert.drive` correctly (cyan modulation ring visible) but rendered as 4 dots on the zero line in the LFOEditor. | ✅ Fixed | 576 |

| 574 | **[Audit] — Resolved by #610] Phase 3 UI Size picker is now live in the SettingsOverlay (Medium / Large). Centring a 75-wide knob in a 73-wide strip produced `s3X = (73 - 75) / 2 = -1`, so every Size-3 knob (`sendEffect`, `sendDelay`, `sendReverb`, `panKnob`, `scAmount`) drew 1 px past each edge — visible clipping across both rhythm-strip dividers. | 559 | **[Feature — Flat scale infrastructure: every layout dimension goes through `mu_ui::s()`; toggling `mu_ui::scale` will scale the whole UI uniformly]** Replaces the cascading approach with the architecture the user asked for. [Source/UI/Components/MuLookAndFeel.h](Source/UI/Components/MuLookAndFeel.h) adds the `mu_ui` namespace with: (1) an inline `scale` global (default 1.0 = Medium); (2) `s(int)` accessor returning `round(N × scale)` for integer pixel values; (3) `sf(float)` for font heights and line widths. Then every panel's `setBounds` and paint coordinate is wrapped in `s()` so when Phase 3 surfaces a Small/Medium/Large picker it just writes a different value to `mu_ui::scale` and the entire UI rescales. Converted panels: [Plugin/PluginEditor.cpp](Source/Plugin/PluginEditor.cpp), [RhythmPanel.cpp](Source/UI/RhythmPanel.cpp), [VoiceSection.cpp](Source/UI/VoiceSection.cpp) (both `resized` and `paint`), [PitchSubsection.cpp](Source/UI/Voice/PitchSubsection.cpp), [FilterSubsection.cpp](Source/UI/Voice/FilterSubsection.cpp), [AmpSubsection.cpp](Source/UI/Voice/AmpSubsection.cpp), [InsertSubsection.cpp](Source/UI/Voice/InsertSubsection.cpp), [EuclideanPanel.cpp](Source/UI/EuclideanPanel.cpp) (both `resized` and `paint`), [MixerChannel.cpp](Source/UI/MixerChannel.cpp), [MixerOverlay.cpp](Source/UI/MixerOverlay.cpp), [FXRow.cpp](Source/UI/FXRow.cpp), [DelayRow.cpp](Source/UI/DelayRow.cpp). Pattern at each call site: `using mu_ui::s; foo.setBounds(s(x), s(y), s(w), s(h));`. At Medium (scale = 1.0) `s()` is the identity — visual output identical to pre-#559. Constants for each panel stay Medium values; "make X bigger" is `change one constant in MuLookAndFeel`; adjacent constants don't move (the user's "no cascading collapse" requirement). 120/120 tests pass. | 550 | **[Feature — Canonical Large knob size scales with plugin window; Euclid Steps/Hits/Rotate and mixer FX rows stay matched at any size]** First-pass fix in #549 used a fixed-pixel `kKnobSizeLarge = 88` on FXRow/DelayRow while leaving Euclid on its responsive `eW = colW * 0.9` formula, which meant the panels diverged whenever the user's standalone window wasn't sitting at exactly the default 1170×870 (Euclid scaled with panel width, FX rows stayed at 88). [Source/UI/FXRow.cpp](Source/UI/FXRow.cpp), [Source/UI/DelayRow.cpp](Source/UI/DelayRow.cpp), [Source/UI/EuclideanPanel.cpp](Source/UI/EuclideanPanel.cpp) all call the helper inside `resized()` for their respective knob widths — so every knob in those three locations now derives its size from the same scale factor and they stay aligned across resizes. Euclid Steps/Hits/Rotate clamp to `innerW / 7` to prevent overflow on very narrow panels. | 548 | **[Bug — Envelope attack time can now be exactly 0]** [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp) `syncEnvelopes()` removed the `kMinAdsrSec = 0.001f` floor from the attack-time argument passed to each `juce::ADSR::setParameters`. Modern JUCE detects `attack == 0` and jumps the envelope straight to peak on noteOn rather than dividing by zero, so the historical floor (added when an older JUCE refused 0) is no longer needed. Decay and release keep a 1 ms floor (zero there would freeze the envelope in those phases). Sustain stays unconstrained (it's amplitude, not time, so 0 was always legal). Attack knobs across pitch/filter/amp already had `setRange(0, ...)` in the UI; the DSP now honours 0 as instant attack instead of clamping to 48 samples of ramp. 120/120 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at build 569. | ✅ Fixed | 569 |

| 544 | **[Bug — EqInsert rewritten with per-sample-smoothed biquad coefficients; zipper noise on Mid-Hz sweep eliminated]** [Source/Audio/FX/Insert/EqInsert.h](Source/Audio/FX/Insert/EqInsert.h) replaced the JUCE `IIR::Filter` cascade (block-rate coefficient swap) with three custom `SmoothBiquad` instances per channel (6 total). Each `SmoothBiquad` carries five `juce::SmoothedValue<float, Linear>` members for its `b0/b1/b2/a1/a2` coefficients, all ramped over 15 ms. Per block: target coefficients are computed from the user knob values via the RBJ Audio EQ Cookbook formulas (peak / low shelf / high shelf) and pushed to the smoothers' `setTargetValue`. Per sample: each coefficient's `getNextValue` is read inside the biquad evaluation (transposed direct form II), so the filter response moves smoothly between samples — coefficient changes never step at block boundaries. First-block-after-prepare uses `setCurrentAndTargetValue` so the EQ snaps to its target response on initial use rather than ramping up from passthrough over 15 ms. Stability: peak/shelf at the Q values used (0.7–1.0) and the user-reachable gain range (±18 dB) keeps poles safely inside the unit circle across every intermediate coefficient set the smoother traverses. The previous per-block-`skip(ns)` dB/Hz smoothing from the earlier fix is no longer needed — replaced by per-sample coefficient smoothing. 120/120 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at build 567. | ✅ Fixed | 567 |

| 538 | **[Audit — EqInsert gain dBs + mid freq smoothed; coefficient swap step reduced ~10×]** [Source/Audio/FX/Insert/EqInsert.h](Source/Audio/FX/Insert/EqInsert.h) added four `SmoothedValue<float, Linear>` members (15 ms ramps) for low dB, high dB, mid dB, mid freq. Per-block: `setTargetValue` from VoiceParams, then `skip(ns)` to advance the smoother by the block and read the smoothed-end value used to recompute biquad coefficients. The change-detection cache (#368) is kept but keyed on *smoothed* values, so the cos/sin/pow recompute still skips once smoothers come to rest. The dual-chain crossfade was considered (audit suggestion) but rejected as more complex than warranted — smoothing the input parameters shrinks per-block dB-steps from "knob speed" to "knob speed / (15 ms / block ms)" (typically ~5–10×), turning audible clicks into soft chuffs. If a user reports residual crackle on aggressive EQ sweeps a follow-up issue can do the proper dual-chain crossfade with internal IIR state copying. 120/120 tests pass. Debug + Release built clean at build 565. | ✅ Fixed | 565 |

| 510 | **[Bug — Karplus-Strong feedback curve changed to cubic for even perceptual spread]** [Source/Audio/FX/Insert/KarplusStrongInsert.h](Source/Audio/FX/Insert/KarplusStrongInsert.h) loop gain mapping changed from linear `fbKnob * 0.9999` to cubic `1 - (1-fbKnob)³`, capped at 0.9999. The linear mapping compressed almost all audible range into the top 20% of the knob (decay time scales as 1/log(gain), so linear spacing produces logarithmic perceptual spacing). Cubic curve spreads the range: 0%=passthrough, 25%≈125ms pluck, 50%≈500ms pluck, 75%≈4s sustain, 100%=near-infinite sustain. Debug + Release built clean. 120/120 tests pass. | ✅ Fixed | 551 |
| 509 | **[Bug — Karplus-Strong loop gain remapped 0..0.9999; default feedback set to 0%]** [Source/Audio/FX/Insert/KarplusStrongInsert.h](Source/Audio/FX/Insert/KarplusStrongInsert.h) loop gain formula changed from `0.95f + fbKnob * 0.05f` to `fbKnob * 0.9999f`. Old mapping (0.95..1.0) meant even at minimum feedback (0%) the string resonated noticeably (~300 ms decay at 48 kHz). New mapping (0..0.9999) gives: 0% = pure passthrough (no resonance), 100% = near-infinite sustain. The audibly interesting pluck range is now ~80–100 %. [Source/UI/InsertAlgoDefaults.h](Source/UI/InsertAlgoDefaults.h) Karplus first-visit default `insertDither` changed from `70.0f` to `0.0f` so the algorithm produces no resonance on first use (consistent with all other insert algorithm defaults). Debug + Release built clean. 120/120 tests pass. | ✅ Fixed | 550 |

| 496 | **[Audit — `/deepaudit` Tier 2 checklist updated with `juce::Timer` dtor pattern]** Added an explicit bullet to the Tier 2 section in [.claude/commands/deepaudit.md](.claude/commands/deepaudit.md): "**`juce::Timer` dtor** — every class deriving from `juce::Timer` must call `stopTimer()` in its destructor; if a timer tick fires during teardown, `timerCallback()` runs on a partially-destroyed object (UAF). Look for `class Foo : ..., private juce::Timer` without a matching `~Foo()` that calls `stopTimer()`." | 479 | **[Housekeeping — .muRhyth presets machine-agnostic: relative sample paths]** All six shipped `.muRhyth` preset files referenced absolute paths (user's personal sample library or OS temp dir), making them unusable on any other machine. Both save sites (`saveRhythmPresetToFile`, `savePreset`) now call `toRelativeSamplePath`; all three preset load sites (`stageRhythmPreset`, `applyRhythmPreset`, `loadPreset`) now call `resolveSamplePath` before the absolute-path fallback. **(2) Preset + sample content fix:** 3 samples copied from personal library, 1 from OS temp to `d:\OneDrive\Documents\TDP\muClid\Samples\` (4 unique files: `01 Kick.wav`, `DT_kick_06.wav`, `12 Canned Snare - FSC Futurephonic.wav`, `11 Floored Open Hat I - FPM Futurephonic.wav`). | 478 | **[Bug — Rhythm hot-swap not staging: no badge, no swap-in — v0 presets]** All six `.muRhyth` preset files in `d:\OneDrive\Documents\TDP\muClid\Rhythms\` were v0 format (no `presetVersion` attribute). `PresetIO::stageRhythmPreset` calls `requireSupportedPresetVersion` at its entry point; when the attribute is absent it defaults `presetVersion` to 0 and returns false, so `hotSwapStager.stage()` was never reached — badge never appeared, swap never committed. | 477 | **[Bug — Mixer insert algorithm clamped to Tape Sat for indices > 10]** [Source/UI/MixerChannel_Bindings.cpp](Source/UI/MixerChannel_Bindings.cpp) `loadFromAPVTS` clamped `mst_insChar` and `mst_ins2Char` APVTS values with `jlimit(0, 10, ...)`. | 472 | **[Housekeeping — Upgrade v0 `.muclid` preset library to v2 format]** All five `.muclid` presets in the user's working library (`Simple Beat`, `Itchy and Scratchy`, `Loving It`, `Testing Preset`, `_default`) were saved in v0 format (JUCE-normalised 0..1 values, no `presetVersion` attribute). After #458 dropped the v0/v1 compat reader and #471 moved the version-check gate ahead of state mutation, every v0 preset was silently rejected on load — the user's entire preset library stopped loading. Fix: new Python script [`tools/upgrade_presets_v0_to_v2.py`](tools/upgrade_presets_v0_to_v2.py) reads each `.muclid`, applies the full v0 → v2 conversion (JUCE `convertFrom0to1` with current APVTS ranges; v0 `migrateLegacyPresetNorm` for `drvChar` / `drvBits` range expansion; algorithm indices → string names per `AlgorithmNames.h` tables; bools → `"true"`/`"false"`; adds `sampleName` from the `sample` path basename when `sampleData` is embedded but `sampleName` was absent), writes the result back atomically, and creates a `.v0_backup` sibling so rollback is always possible. `Dubster.muclid` (already v2) was skipped automatically. | 471 | **[Bug — `loadPreset` version check runs after sequencer resize]** `requireSupportedPresetVersion` was called roughly half-way through `loadPreset`, after the sequencer had already been resized and voice engines re-created to match the incoming preset's rhythm count. A v0 preset would therefore wipe the user's existing rhythm slots (growing/shrinking the sequencer, destroying running VoiceEngine instances, clearing mixer state) before being rejected with the "legacy format" error — leaving the project in a half-loaded default state rather than the pre-load state. Fix: moved `requireSupportedPresetVersion` to the very first action inside the `MuClidPreset` branch, before any sequencer mutation. The check was previously duplicated at the old early-return site (an artefact of the code path); that duplicate was removed. Discovered after #458 rejection messages were silent/dismissed — user loaded a v0 preset, saw no audio, and had to re-add rhythms manually. | ✅ Fixed | 526 |
| 470 | **[Bug — Hot-swap preset load ignores embedded sample, plays silent]** Loading a `.muRhyth` preset while the transport was playing produced UI activity (RhythmCircle animating, sequencer firing) but no audio. Root cause: [`PluginProcessor::stageRhythmPreset`](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp) (the hot-swap entry point) only read the `r0_sample` *path* property and never looked at the `<sampleData>` child element. Presets saved with `embedSample=true` (or auto-embedded via #439's temp-dir detection) write `r0_sample=""` by design — the bytes live in `<sampleData>` — so the hot-swap path silently staged a `VoiceEngine` with no sample. `applyRhythmPreset` (stopped-state entry) had handled both since #439. Fix: mirror `applyRhythmPreset`'s embedded-first / path-second policy in `stageRhythmPreset`. Also added the "linked sample missing" `onLoadError` warning when stored path + same-basename fallback both fail to resolve — previously silent, made the silent-audio case completely unexplained. Discovered by Andy mid-session loading a preset against a running transport. Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 525 |
| 469 | **[Audit — `VoiceSlot`/`Rhythm` copy-op gymnastics removed]** `VoiceSlot` had an explicit copy-constructor and copy-assignment operator to skip copying `mutable std::atomic<bool> modLock` (non-copyable; copies must always start unlocked). `Rhythm` had a matching pair delegating to `VoiceSlot::operator=`. Both were error-prone: any new member added to either class needed manual inclusion in four copy-op bodies. Fix: new `CopyableSpinLock` struct in [Source/Sequencer/VoiceSlot.h](Source/Sequencer/VoiceSlot.h) wraps `std::atomic<bool> v` with copy operations that always produce a new unlocked instance, and forwards `.exchange`/`.store`/`.compare_exchange_strong` so all call sites are unchanged. `VoiceSlot::modLock` type changed from `std::atomic<bool>` to `CopyableSpinLock`; both `VoiceSlot` and `Rhythm` drop their explicit copy-ops entirely (compiler-generated ops are now correct). The one site that took `&r->modLock` as `std::atomic<bool>*` ([Source/UI/ModulatorPanel.cpp:70](Source/UI/ModulatorPanel.cpp#L70)) updated to `&r->modLock.v`. `Rhythm : public VoiceSlot` inheritance preserved — composition refactor deferred (would ripple across 24 files with no functional benefit at current stage). Debug + Release built clean. | ✅ Fixed | 542 |

| 446 | **[Branding bug — follow-up to #421]** Standalone window title bar showed `?-Clid` instead of `μ-Clid` (Greek lowercase mu, U+03BC, UTF-8 `0xCE 0xBC`). **Root cause:** `getApplicationName()` returned `juce::CharPointer_UTF8(JucePlugin_Name)` ([StandaloneApp.cpp:87](Source/StandaloneApp.cpp#L87)), where `JucePlugin_Name` is the macro `"μ-Clid"` defined by JUCE's CMake helper. That macro reaches MSVC via the `-D JucePlugin_Name="μ-Clid"` command-line argument — and the cmd/console host re-encodes multibyte characters through the system codepage en route, so the μ byte pair gets mojibake'd into `?` before the compiler ever sees it. Same root cause as the mojibake'd Inno-Setup console output noted in #421. **Fix:** hard-code the UTF-8 byte sequence `"\xce\xbc-Clid"` inside `getApplicationName()` so the title bytes come directly from source rather than via the CMake → MSVC `-D` round-trip. `MUCLID_LITE_BUILD` guard selects `"\xce\xbc-Clid Lite"` for the Lite standalone. Matches the existing escape used on [StandaloneApp.cpp:27](Source/StandaloneApp.cpp#L27) for the "Close μ-Clid?" dialog. Settings filename at [:76](Source/StandaloneApp.cpp#L76) (uses `JucePlugin_Name` for the `.settings` filename — only ever appears on disk, not in any user-visible chrome) left as-is — even if mangled, it just changes the filename `?-Clid.settings` which still works as a filesystem path on Windows. Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 513 |

| 444 | **[Phase 2 for #423 Vocoder]** Three Vocoder Phase-2 items landed. **(1) Modulation destinations — `voc.note` / `voc.octave` / `voc.unison`** added to `ModDest::kTable` ([ModulatorEditor.h](Source/UI/ModulatorEditor.h)) at indices 41–43. `ModDest::populate()` case 12 now exposes them under a "Vocoder" section heading in the destination dropdown. `depthScaleFor` ([ModulationMatrix.cpp:71-78](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp#L71)) returns 6 / 4 / 6 so depth=100% × src=100% spans the full integer range (note 0..6, octave 1..5, unison 0..6). [`PluginProcessor::processBlock`](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L518) modulation pass seeds the new dest paramValues from voiceParams when `driveChar == 12` (`voc.note = drvBits - 1`, `voc.octave = drvDither`, `voc.unison = (driveOutput + 24) / 4` so the user-facing 0..6 unison index is what the matrix actually offsets); after the matrix runs, the write-back ([PluginProcessor.cpp:644-651](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L644)) clamps each back to its algorithm range and re-encodes unison (`vIdx * 4 - 24`) into the driveOutput storage. Other algorithms (driveChar != 12) pay zero matrix-process cost since their `voc.*` entries stay at 0 and the dropdown doesn't expose them. **(2) UI grey-out for noise carriers.** When Vocoder's Wave knob is set to White (2) or Pink (3), the Note / Octave / Unison knobs are now `setEnabled(false)` + `setAlpha(0.45f)` so the user can see they're inactive. Implemented in both the per-rhythm Voice page ([VoiceSection.cpp](Source/UI/VoiceSection.cpp) case 12) and the mixer master-insert page ([MixerChannel_Insert.cpp](Source/UI/MixerChannel_Insert.cpp) case 12). The Wave knob's `onValueChanged` re-runs the grey-out sync each time, so live waveshape changes update the disabled state immediately. `configureInsertAlgorithm` resets enabled=true on all four insert knobs at function entry, so switching FROM Vocoder back to a different algorithm doesn't inherit the grey state. **(3) Voice-entry gain ramp on Unison-up.** Added `voiceGainSmooth[kMaxUnisonVoices]` per-voice state to `VocoderInsert` ([VocoderInsert.h](Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/VocoderInsert.h)). Each sample, every voice's smoothed gain ramps exponentially (~5 ms time constant via `kEntryRampMs`) toward its target — `voiceGain[v]` for v < unisonN, 0 for v >= unisonN. The carrier sum uses `voiceGainSmooth[v]` instead of `voiceGain[v]` directly. Result: turning the Unison knob UP makes new voices fade in over 5 ms instead of snapping in at full level. Also smooths Unison-DOWN (voices that just left the active range fade out instead of cutting). `reset()` zeroes the array so `markRetired()` / hot-swap don't inherit stale gain envelopes. Pitched carriers only — the noise-carrier path doesn't use per-voice gains. Built Debug + Release clean. Phase-2 stereo-aware analysis split off as #445. | ✅ Fixed | 512 |
| 443 | **[Phase 2 for #422 Karplus-Strong]** Modulation destinations and the LPF / damping control are both done. **(1) Modulation destinations — `ks.note` / `ks.octave`** added to `ModDest::kTable` ([ModulatorEditor.h](Source/UI/ModulatorEditor.h)) at indices 39–40. `ModDest::populate()` case 11 (Karplus) now exposes them under a "Karplus" section heading along with `insert.dither` (= the Feedback knob, already continuous and naturally moddable) and `insert.lpf` (= the new LPF knob added in #428). `depthScaleFor` ([ModulationMatrix.cpp:71-72](Source/Modulation/ModulationMatrix.cpp#L71)) returns 6 / 3 so depth=100% × src=100% spans the full chromatic range (0..6 notes) or full octave range (0..3). | 439 | **[Audit — Embedded sample temp-path leaks into re-saves]** The save path now detects samples loaded from the embedded-sample decode temp dir (`%TEMP%/muClid_samples/`) and force-embeds them rather than writing the ephemeral temp path as `r0_sample`. Both paths surface the auto-embed via `onLoadError` so the user knows their explicit "don't embed" choice was overridden — the alternative was a silently-broken preset that loses the sample on next OS reboot. | 430 | **[Bug — preset back-compat]** Loading any `.muRhyth` / `.muclid` preset saved before #422/#423 reinterpreted `drvChar` and `drvBits` against the new wider ranges, shifting integer algorithm selectors up. Symptom (user-reported): default preset works fine; switching to a "more complex preset" plays white-ish hash on every hit; subsequent preset switches stay noisy. **Root cause:** preset files store `param->getValue()` (normalised 0..1). When the APVTS range for `drvChar` was widened 0..10 → 0..12 in #422/#423, an old normalised 1.0 (TapeSat=10) now resolves to 12 → Vocoder. Whatever `drvDrv` (0..100) the legacy TapeSat preset held got read as Vocoder waveshape — clamped to 0..3, so anything ≥ 67 % loads as **Pink Noise carrier** = noise on every hit. Same shift applies to `drvBits` (1..16 → 0..16 in #429) and to the master inserts `mst_insChar` / `mst_ins2Char` / `mst_insBits` / `mst_ins2Bits`. The default preset works only because `drvChar=0` is a fixpoint under any range. **Fix:** added `kCurrentPresetVersion = 1` + `migrateLegacyPresetNorm(suffix, norm)` / `migrateLegacyGlobalNorm(id, norm)` helpers in [PluginProcessor_Internal.h](Source/PluginProcessor_Internal.h). All four load paths — `applyRhythmPreset` ([PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp:281](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp#L281), stopped-mode `.muRhyth`), `stageRhythmPreset` ([:32](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp#L32), playing-mode `.muRhyth` hot-swap), `loadPreset` ([:873](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp#L873), `.muclid` rhythm tree + GlobalState child) — read `state.getProperty("presetVersion", 0)`. If absent or below `kCurrentPresetVersion`, each normalised value is run through the migrator before `setValueNotifyingHost` / `convertFrom0to1`. Migration math: `drvChar` legacy → current `newNorm = oldNorm * 10/12` (so a value V in 0..10 resolves back to V); `drvBits` legacy → current `newNorm = (1 + oldNorm * 15) / 16`. All four save paths — `saveRhythmPreset`, `saveRhythmPresetToFile`, `savePreset` (the two .muRhyth writers + the .muclid writer) — now tag the file with `presetVersion = kCurrentPresetVersion`, so any preset newly saved on this build skips the migration on next load. **Host-state path (DAW project state) was already correct:** APVTS's state-tree stores de-normalised actual values, not normalised, so range widening doesn't shift values there — confirmed by inspection of `migrateLegacyHostState` and `apvts.replaceState` semantics. Built Debug + Release clean. **Test plan:** (1) open standalone, load a pre-#422 preset that used TapeSat or Limiter — should now sound correct (was: noise). (2) open standalone, switch through several pre-#422 presets — should each sound correct. (3) save a new preset, reload it — should sound correct (verifies new-format saves migrate to themselves correctly). (4) any `.muclid` full preset saved before #422 should load with correct master-insert algorithms. | ✅ Fixed | 510 |
| 429 | **[Bug + features]** Three user-visible fixes in one build. **(1) Mixer: Delay return showed a Delay send (self-feedback knob).** Same for Reverb return → Reverb send. Visibility logic at [MixerChannel.cpp:200-202](Source/UI/MixerChannel.cpp#L200) used `channelType != Type::ReverbReturn` for sendDelay (so it hid only on ReverbReturn, not on DelayReturn) and an unconditional show for sendReverb. Octave 0 = SPN C1 = 32.7 Hz (bottom of audible range). Lowest pitch is now Octave 0 + Note C = 32.7 Hz → delay buffer cap bumped from 1024 to 2048 samples in `prepare()` to fit. Pitch formula changed from `kLowestFreq(65.4) * 2^((semi + 12*(oct-1))/12)` to `kLowestFreq(32.7) * 2^((semi + 12*oct)/12)` so existing presets with Octave 1/2/3 still play at the same frequencies as before (only added Octave 0 below). APVTS `drvBits` min lowered from 1 → 0 (both per-rhythm `drvBits` and master inserts `mst_insBits` / `mst_ins2Bits`) so storing 0 doesn't clamp to 1 — Bitcrusher still uses 1..16 inside its case, the wider range just allows other algorithms to use 0. **(3) Vocoder: octave range shifted down by one.** `kLowestFreq` in [VocoderInsert.h](Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/VocoderInsert.h) changed 65.4 → 32.7 Hz. Octave knob range stays 1..5 but now maps to SPN octaves 1..5 (was 2..6). Same musical span, just an octave lower overall — gives access to deeper bass-region carrier frequencies. Built Debug + Release clean. Deployed to OneDrive tester folder. | ✅ Fixed | 507 |
| 428 | **[#422/#423 bug fixes + deploy hardening]** Three reported bugs in the new insert effects, plus a build-script improvement. **(1) Karplus Feedback didn't reach max sustain:** loop gain was capped at 0.999 (`0.95 + fbKnob * (0.999 - 0.95)`). Bumped to reach 1.0 at full knob — the LP filter in the feedback path always removes some energy per cycle, so the loop is stable at 1.0 without explosive growth. Below 0.95 the string still dies in a few ms; above that the user now has full control over the long-sustain range. [KarplusStrongInsert.h:80](Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/KarplusStrongInsert.h#L80). **(2) Karplus LPF control:** previously the feedback-path LP cutoff was hardcoded at 4× target freq. Now exposed as a 4th UI knob ("LPF") wired to `driveTone` (20 Hz – 20 kHz log range, same as other inserts' LPF knob). Lower cutoff = darker / quicker decay; 20 kHz effectively bypasses the LP so the feedback gain alone shapes the envelope. UI knob added in both [VoiceSection.cpp](Source/UI/VoiceSection.cpp) and [MixerChannel_Insert.cpp](Source/UI/MixerChannel_Insert.cpp) case 11. **(3) Vocoder unison stuck at 13 voices + reset on note change:** root cause was the unison index 0..6 being stored in `driveTone`, whose APVTS range is 20..20000. When the snapshot system tried `apvtsSet("drvTon", 1.0)` for the default unison index 1, JUCE clamped to 20.0. The algorithm's `juce::jlimit(0, 6, (int)20.0)` then yielded 6 → 13 voices. Every parameterChanged-triggered `configureInsertAlgorithm` re-read this stuck 20.0 and reset the unison knob. **Fix:** moved unison storage from `driveTone` to `driveOutput` (range -24..0, which freely holds the encoded value `unisonIdx * 4 - 24`). Algorithm reads `juce::jlimit(0, 6, (int)((p.driveOutput + 24) / 4))`. UI knob value (0..6) encodes via `v * 4 - 24` on write. Frees up `driveTone` for the Note label — the existing Note storage in `drvBits` now drives the "Note" knob shown in the leftover `extra` UI slot. [VocoderInsert.h:50](Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/VocoderInsert.h#L50). **(4) Build-script hardening:** the OneDrive deploy step at [cmake/DeployRelease.cmake](cmake/DeployRelease.cmake) was aborting the entire build if any destination file was locked (user running the standalone, antivirus scan mid-build, OneDrive sync). Wrapped each `file(COPY_FILE)` with `RESULT` capture (and the VST3 bundle copy with `execute_process(... copy_directory)` since `file(COPY)` lacks a result-capture variant), downgrading lock-failures to warnings. The build now completes and the user gets a clear message ("close any running μ-Clid") instead of an MSB3073 wall. **Default values updated** in kInsertDefaults[11/12] in both [VoiceSection.cpp](Source/UI/VoiceSection.cpp) and [MixerChannel_Insert.cpp](Source/UI/MixerChannel_Insert.cpp): Karplus now defaults driveTone=20000 (LPF wide open); Vocoder defaults driveOutput=-20 (unison index 1 = 3 voices). Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 506 |
| 427 | **[Refactor]** [MultiModeFilter](Source/Audio/MultiModeFilter.cpp) migrated from a single 200-line if/else cascade over `typeCodeValue` into a class-per-algorithm dispatch table mirroring #425 / #426. New folder [Source/Audio/Processing/Filters/](Source/Audio/Processing/Filters/) contains `FilterAlgorithmBase.h` (abstract base — `prepare/reset/process(cutoffHz, resonance)`) plus 16 concrete algorithm headers — one per dropdown entry, named after what the user sees in the UI: `Lp12Filter`, `Hp12Filter`, `Bp12Filter`, `Notch12Filter`, `Lp24Filter`, `Hp24Filter`, `Bp24Filter`, `Lp6Filter`, `CombPlusFilter`, `Ap12Filter`, `Notch24Filter`, `Hp6Filter`, `PeakFilter`, `LowShelfFilter`, `HighShelfFilter`, `CombMinusFilter`. Naming policy: each file describes the FILTER TYPE, not the underlying DSP primitive — so "looking up LP24 in the code" is a direct one-step lookup (`Lp24Filter.h`) instead of "I think 24dB filters use Ladder, let me find that". Each class owns its own DSP state (`StateVariableTPTFilter`, `LadderFilter`, `BiquadFilter`, `OnePoleLP`/`OnePoleHP`, or comb delay buffer + write pointer). `MultiModeFilter` itself shrinks from 80 lines of `.h` + 200 lines of `.cpp` to 60 lines of `.h` + 65 lines of `.cpp`; it's now just an orchestrator that pre-allocates `std::array<std::unique_ptr<FilterAlgorithmBase>, 16>` in the constructor and dispatches via `algorithms[typeCode]->process(...)`. **Public API unchanged** — `prepare/reset/setType/setCutoff/setResonance/process` signatures identical, so [VoiceEngine](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp)'s `voiceFilter` member needs no edits. **Trade-off accepted:** previously SVF-family modes (LP12/HP12/BP12/Notch12) shared a single internal SVF instance — switching between them carried the integrator state across. Now each has its own SVF (and similarly each Ladder mode has its own Ladder, each biquad-mode has its own biquad). Practical effect: switching filter type mid-tone briefly loses the previous filter's state. The SVF integrators settle in microseconds, the Ladder topology smooths internally, and the comb pair share nothing anyway — so the audible difference is negligible. The win is that filter type lookup is now a 1:1 file mapping, and adding a 17th filter mode in the future is a drop-in new file + one line in the constructor + one entry in the APVTS dropdown choice list. **Per-mode coefficient-recompute skip preserved:** the #368 change-detection cache (`lastCutoffHz` / `lastResonance` per algorithm) is now per-class state instead of a shared cache on MultiModeFilter — every algorithm that benefits (Lp6/Hp6/Ap12/Peak/LowShelf/HighShelf) carries its own. `CMakeLists.txt` unchanged — `MultiModeFilter.cpp` was already on the source list; the new headers propagate via include chain. Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 499 |
| 426 | **[Cleanup]** Reorganised the audio processing folder layout so the two algorithm collections live side by side under one parent, making the "they're both just processing algorithms" relationship obvious from the filesystem. **Moves:** `Source/Audio/Insert/` → `Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/` (11 files: `InsertAlgorithmBase.h` + 10 algorithm headers from #425); `Source/FX/Effects/` → `Source/Audio/Processing/SendFX/` (5 files: `EffectAlgorithmBase.h` + 4 algorithm headers — Chorus / Flanger / Phaser / Echo). **Kept in place:** `Source/FX/FXAlgorithmDef.h` (the algorithm metadata struct — referenced by both SendFX algorithm headers AND the orchestration layer in `FX/EffectSlot.h` / `FX/ReverbSlot.h`, plus several unrelated callers in PluginProcessor and UI; moving it would force longer #include paths in those orchestration files); all other `Source/FX/*` files (FXChain, FXSlotBase, OversampledProcessor, EffectSlot, DelaySlot, ReverbSlot — these are the orchestration layer that own the algorithm instances); `Source/Audio/InsertProcessor.{h,cpp}` (mirror role to FX/EffectSlot — the per-voice orchestrator that drives the InsertFX algorithms via the #425 dispatch table). **Include paths updated:** all internal references inside the moved files switched from relative (`"../VoiceParams.h"`, `"../FXAlgorithmDef.h"`, `"../AudioFilters.h"`) to absolute-from-Source (`"Audio/VoiceParams.h"`, `"FX/FXAlgorithmDef.h"`, `"Audio/AudioFilters.h"`) — possible because the project already has `Source/` on the `mu-core` interface include path. No source files were added or removed (the cpp source list still points at `Source/Audio/InsertProcessor.cpp`; the moved files are header-only and propagate via include chain). Built Debug + Release clean. Net effect: a developer looking for "what insert / send FX algorithms exist?" can now answer with one `ls Source/Audio/Processing/` instead of having to know about two unrelated-looking subtrees under different parents. | ✅ Fixed | 497 |
| 425 | **[Refactor]** Insert effects migrated from a single ~300-line switch statement in [InsertProcessor.cpp](Source/Audio/InsertProcessor.cpp) into a class-per-algorithm dispatch table, mirroring the FX-rack pattern in [Source/FX/Effects/](Source/FX/Effects/). New folder [Source/Audio/Insert/](Source/Audio/Insert/) contains: `InsertAlgorithmBase.h` (abstract base — `prepare/reset/process`, no oversampling or send-mode unlike `EffectAlgorithmBase` since inserts run inside the voice's per-sample inner loop), plus 10 concrete algorithm headers (`NoneInsert`, `SoftClipInsert`, `HardClipInsert`, `FoldInsert`, `BitcrusherInsert`, `ClipperInsert`, `EqInsert`, `CompressorLimiterInsert`, `RingModInsert`, `TapeSatInsert`). All header-only / inline since most algorithms are 20–40 LOC and pulling them into `.cpp` files would force a CMake source-list edit per algorithm. `InsertProcessor` now: (a) holds `std::vector<std::unique_ptr<InsertAlgorithmBase>> owned` reserved to `kNumAlgorithms` at ctor so the raw pointers it stores in `dispatch[]` stay stable across `push_back` calls; (b) `std::array<InsertAlgorithmBase*, 11> dispatch` maps driveChar (0..10) → owned algorithm. **Comp/Lim sharing preserved:** indices 7 (Compressor) and 8 (Limiter) alias the SAME `CompressorLimiterInsert` instance — bit-identical to the pre-refactor switch-case behaviour where both driveChar codes operated on the same `compEnvelope[2]` member (switching between Comp and Limiter mid-bar carries the envelope state across instead of resetting it; the ratio selection is read per-call from `p.driveChar`). **Post-drive tone filter kept in InsertProcessor itself** rather than distributed to each algorithm — it's a property of the drive-family (driveChar < 6 uses p.driveTone as a 1-pole LP cutoff; cases 6+ repurpose driveTone), not of any single algorithm's DSP. Each algorithm's state is now encapsulated in its own class: `prevDriveX[]` → `SoftClipInsert::xPrev` + `HardClipInsert::xPrev` (two independent instances, fine since the switch couldn't be active for both at once anyway); `bitAaFilter`/`bitRateCounter`/`bitRateHeld`/`rng` → `BitcrusherInsert`; `compEnvelope` → `CompressorLimiterInsert::envelope`; `ringPhase` → `RingModInsert::phase`; `dcBlockIn`/`dcBlockOut` → `TapeSatInsert::dcIn/dcOut`; the 3 EQ filters + their `eqLast*` change-detection cache → `EqInsert`. Public API (`prepare/reset/process` + `grReduction` atomic) unchanged so external callers ([VoiceEngine::insertProc](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp), [MixerEngine::masterInsert](Source/Audio/MixerEngine.h), `VoiceSection::driveOutput.setGRSource`) need no changes. CMakeLists.txt unchanged — InsertProcessor.cpp was already listed, the new headers propagate via include chain. Built Debug + Release clean (only pre-existing C4566 μ-character warnings from StandaloneApp.cpp, unrelated). Net delta: `InsertProcessor.cpp` shrinks from ~300 to ~85 lines; each algorithm gets a focused 30–80 line file with its own state. Adding Karplus–Strong (#422) and Vocoder (#423) is now drop-in: one new header in `Source/Audio/Insert/` + one line in the InsertProcessor ctor + the existing `configureInsertAlgorithm` UI plumbing. Behaviour preservation verified by construction: every case's body was extracted verbatim, the post-drive filter gating logic is identical, the Comp/Lim shared-state behaviour preserved via dispatch aliasing. | ✅ Fixed | 495 |

| 423 | **[Feature]** Insert effect **Vocoder** — driveChar = 12. New class [VocoderInsert.h](Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/VocoderInsert.h). 20-band parallel vocoder: analysis biquad bandpass on mono down-mixed input → one-pole envelope follower (5 ms attack / 30 ms release) → multiplies a matching synthesis biquad on the carrier; band outputs summed; result broadcast to both channels. Band centres log-spaced 80 Hz – 10 kHz at Q≈5 using the project's existing `BiquadFilter` (no new DSP primitive). **Carrier:** four waveshape options (Saw / Square / White Noise / Pink Noise via Paul Kellet's filter). Pitched carriers (Saw / Square) use SPN-anchored pitch from C@Oct1=65.4 Hz (same convention as #422). **Unison:** up to 13 parallel detuned phase accumulators (1/3/5/7/9/11/13 voices) with symmetric placement around the centre frequency; spread `D(N) = 0/8/16/24/32/40/50 cents`; per-voice gain falloff `1 - 0.6 * |pos|/D(N)` so outer voices sit at 0.4× the centre; total output normalised by `1/sum(gain)` so loudness is consistent across unison settings. Phase-continuous oscillators mean no click on frequency change. **Param encoding (driveChar=12):** `driveDrive` = waveshape 0..3, `drvBits` = note index+1 (1..7 → C..B), `drvDither` = octave 1..5, `driveTone` = unison index 0..6. UI knobs step in integer increments and display the readable label (note letter, octave number, voice count, waveshape name) via `textFromValueFunction`. Registered in [InsertProcessor.cpp](Source/Audio/InsertProcessor.cpp) (kNumAlgorithms 11→13); dropdowns in `VoiceSection` and `MixerChannel` get a "Vocoder" item; `configureInsertAlgorithm` cases added in both. CPU is non-trivial (40 biquads + 20 envelope followers + N≤13 phase accumulators per voice per sample) — usable but a candidate for "high-CPU FX" categorisation later. Phase 2 work tracked in #423-followups: modulation destinations, noise-carrier UI grey-out, voice-entry gain ramp on Unison-up, stereo-aware analysis. Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 501 |
| 422 | **[Feature]** Insert effect **Karplus–Strong** — driveChar = 11. New class [KarplusStrongInsert.h](Source/Audio/Processing/InsertFX/KarplusStrongInsert.h). Classic K-S loop: short circular delay line (sized for lowest pitch C@Oct1=65.4 Hz → 1024 samples capacity at 48 kHz prepare time, so a sample-rate change up to ~89 kHz fits without realloc) plus a one-pole LP inside the feedback path. Excites with the incoming voice signal so each trigger plucks the string. Linear-interpolated fractional delay reads + `juce::SmoothedValue<float>` on `target_freq` with ~15 ms ramp means pitch changes (knob or future modulation) turn into a fast smooth slide instead of a phase-discontinuity click. **Pitch math (SPN-anchored at C=65.4 Hz for Octave 1):** notes ascend C→B chromatically with semitone offsets 0/2/4/5/7/9/11; octave-knob position N maps to SPN octave (N+1). LP cutoff in the feedback path auto-tracks at 4× target freq for natural high-frequency damping. **Param encoding (driveChar=11):** `driveDrive` = note index 0..6, `drvBits` = octave 1..3, `drvDither` = feedback 0..100% mapped internally to loop gain 0.95..0.999. UI knobs step in integers and display via `textFromValueFunction` (note letter, octave number, feedback %). Registered in [InsertProcessor.cpp](Source/Audio/InsertProcessor.cpp) (kNumAlgorithms 11→13 — shared bump with #423); dropdowns in [VoiceSection.cpp](Source/UI/VoiceSection.cpp) and [MixerChannel.cpp](Source/UI/MixerChannel.cpp) get a "Karplus" item; `configureInsertAlgorithm` cases added in both. APVTS `drvChar` integer range bumped 0..10 → 0..12 in both per-rhythm and master-insert (`mst_insChar` / `mst_ins2Char`) parameter declarations, plus the `applyRhythmSuffix` `jlimit`. Trivial CPU compared with the vocoder. Phase 2 work tracked in #422-followups: modulation destinations, damping control exposure. Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 501 |

| 420 | **[Bug]** Envelope Attack knob (and any other ADSR time knob) set to 0 visibly crept up by a tiny amount as soon as another envelope control was touched. Symptom was the slider re-displaying 0.001 instead of 0 — audio effect inaudible at that resolution, but the visual was wrong. Root cause: `applyRhythmSuffix` in [PluginProcessor_Internal.h](Source/PluginProcessor_Internal.h) applied `juce::jmax(0.001f, v)` to all six ADSR time fields (`pEnvAtk/Dec/Rel`, `fEnvAtk/Dec/Rel`, `aEnvAtk/Dec/Rel`) before writing them into `voiceParams`. The floor existed because JUCE's `ADSR::Parameters` struct rejects zero — but it was being applied in the WRONG layer (the data layer that the UI reads from). An APVTS value of 0 round-tripped through `voiceParams.ampEnvAtk` as 0.001; when an unrelated parameterChanged fired and triggered `VoiceSection::refreshSuffix`, the slider read back the floored 0.001 and visibly bumped off the floor. Fix: removed the floor from all six setters in `applyRhythmSuffix` so `voiceParams` faithfully stores the user's chosen value; moved the floor INTO `VoiceEngine::syncEnvelopes` at [VoiceEngine.cpp:288-308](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L288) where it's applied inline on each `setParameters(...)` time arg via `juce::jmax(kMinAdsrSec=0.001f, ...)`. Sustains are amplitude (not time) so they pass through unchanged — 0 sustain is a legitimate user choice (the "silence after decay" semantic, see #417). Audio-thread modulation path at [PluginProcessor.cpp:605-612](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L605) already applied the floor when building per-block `modParams` — left as-is (that path writes to a local, not back to voiceParams, so it can't cause UI creep). Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 490 |
| 419 | **[Feature]** Pattern-aware legato for the sequencer. **Problem:** every step that fires a hit called `VoiceEngine::trigger()` → `ampEnv.noteOn()`. The existing #221 per-envelope `ampEnvLegato` / `filterEnvLegato` / `pitchEnvLegato` flags only chose "reset env to 0 vs continue from current level" before `noteOn` — `noteOn` always fired, so Attack always restarted on every step. Effect: envelope time was capped by step length. A 4s decay could never breathe past one step before the next hit interrupted it. **Solution:** new per-rhythm **Pattern Legato** mode. When enabled, the sequencer marks "tied" hits — adjacent steps that are both hits with no rest between — and the audio engine skips the envelope retrigger on those hits. The sample voice still retriggers on every hit (rhythmic pulse preserved); a short linear fade-in ramps the sample-voice restart against the running envelope tail to avoid the waveform-discontinuity click. **Implementation:** (a) `Rhythm` gains `bool patternLegato` at [Source/Sequencer/Rhythm.h:55](Source/Sequencer/Rhythm.h#L55) (copy/copy-assign updated). (b) `BlockResult` gains `int tiedMask` at [Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.h:7](Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.h#L7); always populated. (c) `SequencerEngine` tracks `wasLastStepHit[MaxRhythms]` per audio-thread state, set/cleared per step walked in `processBlock` at [SequencerEngine.cpp:283-322](Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.cpp#L283); reset to false alongside `lastStepIndex = -1` in `resetStepTrackingForSwap` / `removeRhythm` / `setNumRhythms` so post-swap / post-shrink rhythms never see a stale tied bit. (d) `VoiceEngine::trigger(bool isAccented, bool tied)` at [VoiceEngine.cpp:70-100](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L70) — when `tied` is true, skip all three `env.reset() / env.noteOn()` blocks (env continues uninterrupted); always pass `fadeInSamples` to `SamplePlayer::trigger` (64 samples ≈ 1.3 ms @ 48k for tied, 0 for untied to preserve drum transients). (e) `SamplePlayer::trigger(int fadeInSamples)` at [SamplePlayer.cpp:5](Source/Audio/SamplePlayer.cpp#L5) — publishes the fade length atomically alongside the triggered flag; `process()` applies a per-sample linear ramp `1 - remaining/total → 1.0` over `fadeInSamples` then runs at unity. (f) `PluginProcessor::processBlock` trigger call at [PluginProcessor.cpp:421-431](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L421) gates the tied bit on `getRhythm(r).patternLegato` so the flag controls the behaviour; tiedMask itself is always computed (cheap — one branch per step). (g) APVTS: new `r{i}_patLeg` boolean param registered at [PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp:99](Source/PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp#L99); push/pull wired through `kRhythmSuffixes`, `applyRhythmSuffix`, and `pushRhythmToAPVTS` so the flag persists in host state and `.muRhyth` preset files. (h) UI: new `legatoCtrl` 2-segment SegmentControl `{"Trig","Leg"}` in `EuclideanPanel`, placed FIRST on the logic row with an 8 px sub-panel divider before the existing logic pills. Layout constants (`kLegatoW`, `kLogicGapW`, `kLogicMP`) hoisted to the header so `resized()` and `paint()` stay in sync; `paint()` draws two separate rounded-rect outlines for the sub-panel look. `loadFromRhythm` + `refreshSuffix("patLeg")` keep the toggle in sync with preset loads + parameter changes. Built Debug + Release clean. **Test plan (user listening):** (1) set sustain=0, decay=4s, dense pattern with adjacent hits → with Trig: envelope retriggers every step (no decay tail); with Leg: contiguous hits keep the envelope alive so the 4s decay breathes across the run. (2) Tied hit immediately after a rest should retrigger normally (rest broke the tie). (3) Pad / pluck samples should not click on tied hits (1.3 ms fade-in does its job); transient drum sounds should remain transient when Pattern Legato is off (zero fade-in path). | ✅ Fixed | 487 |
