| 417 | **[Envelope bug — pre-existing, surfaced during Stage 34 listening]** With Release knob at max (`ampRelToEnd = true`), the amp envelope was being skipped entirely — not just during the release phase. Symptom: Sustain=0 + Decay=4s + a long pad sample → user expected the sample to silence after 4s of decay, but it played at full level forever. Root cause at [VoiceEngine.cpp:140](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L140): the prior gate `if (!activeParams.ampRelToEnd) ampEnv.applyEnvelopeToBuffer(...)` treated "release-to-end" as "bypass the envelope entirely" rather than its intended meaning of "let the sample play through on RELEASE instead of fading over the release time." Since this codebase never calls `noteOff` during normal play (drum-style trigger model — env holds in Sustain forever after each hit), the env's release phase only happens for Stage 34 retired engines via `markRetired()`. So the `ampRelToEnd` gate's job is to control behaviour at noteOff, not at applyEnvelopeToBuffer. Fix: unconditionally apply the envelope in `process()`. The "release-to-end" semantic now lives entirely in `markRetired()` at [VoiceEngine.cpp:165](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L165) — when `ampRelToEnd == true`, the amp env is NOT noteOff'd, so it stays at its current value (sustain level, or wherever decay left it) and `applyEnvelopeToBuffer` keeps multiplying by that level → sample plays through to its natural end at the user-set sustain volume. When `ampRelToEnd == false`, `noteOff` fires as before → env enters release → sample fades over the user's release time. `isFullyDrained()` updated at [VoiceEngine.cpp:189](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L189) to handle the new mode: for retired ampRelToEnd engines (where amp env never reaches idle because there's no noteOff), drain on voices-finished alone — the sample running out is the sole signal that the engine has nothing left to render. User's scenario after fix: trigger → attack peaks → decay over 4s down to sustain=0 → sample silent thereafter (env still ticks during sustain hold, multiplying buffer by 0). Hot-swap during decay: env continues decaying naturally; sample plays through to natural end at whatever the env value reaches; engine drains. Filter / pitch envelopes still get noteOff'd in markRetired regardless of ampRelToEnd — they don't have a release-to-end equivalent. Built Debug + Release clean. | ✅ Fixed | 486 |
| 416 | **[Stage 34 Step 3 fix]** Retired engines were producing an audible "effect overlay" (comb-filter ring / bitcrusher tail) on the new active rhythm — symptom: load a comb-filter / bitcrusher preset, play, swap to a clean kick preset, the kick sounds like it's going through the previous preset's effects. Two compounding causes, both now fixed: **(1) Engines never drained.** `juce::ADSR::isActive()` returns true throughout Attack/Decay/Sustain/Release and only goes false in IDLE. The codebase never calls `noteOff()` anywhere (drum-style trigger model — sample plays through, amp env holds in Sustain forever). So `isFullyDrained()` checked `ampEnv.isActive() == false`, which was never true post-trigger → retired slot leaked, engine rendered until plugin destruction. **(2) Filter / insert state kept ringing.** `VoiceEngine::process()` applies amp env BEFORE the filter, but the final `output.addFrom(... ampLevel * accentGain)` does NOT include amp env. So a high-feedback comb filter's delay line (or compressor envelope / DC-block / bitrate-hold from the InsertProcessor) kept self-feeding into the channel buffer at full amp level even after the sample finished — independent of the amp envelope state. Fix: added `VoiceEngine::markRetired() noexcept` at [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h:50](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h#L50) / [.cpp:165](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L165). Calls `noteOff()` on amp/filter/pitch envelopes (so amp env progresses Sustain → Release → Idle and the drain check eventually fires) AND `voiceFilter.reset()` + `insertProc.reset()` (clears comb buffers, ladder/SVF state, compressor envelope, ringmod phase, DC-block, bitrate accumulators — eliminates the audible overlay without touching the SamplePlayer voices or the amp env's release phase, which together are the legitimate "sample + envelope tail" Stage 34 is supposed to give). `handleAsyncUpdate`'s retire path at [PluginProcessor.cpp:1077](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L1077) calls `oldEngine->markRetired()` BEFORE placing the engine into the retired slot (still under suspendProcessing, so direct state mutation is safe — audio thread cannot be mid-`process()`). **Secondary fix at [VoiceEngine.cpp:144-156](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L144):** when `ampRelToEnd == true`, amp env was never `applyEnvelopeToBuffer`'d → never ticked → a retired ampRelToEnd engine would sit in Release forever and never drain. Added an explicit per-sample `getNextSample()` tick gated on `retired == true` so the release progresses without applying the env to the buffer (preserves ampRelToEnd's "let the sample play through unscaled" intent for the sample audio). Built Debug + Release clean. User-facing test: 3.1 listening verification confirmed clean-kick-after-comb-preset symptom is the next thing to check. | ✅ Fixed | 485 |
| 415 | **[Stage 34 Step 3]** Retire-on-swap — the actual user-facing seamless hot-swap feature. Modified `handleAsyncUpdate`'s swap-commit block at [Source/PluginProcessor.cpp:1051-1095](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L1051): the prior `voiceEngines[r] = std::move(sw.pendingVoice)` (which silently destroyed the old engine mid-render) now does retire-then-swap. The old engine is `std::move`d into a local `oldEngine`, the new engine moves into the active slot, then `oldEngine` is placed into the first empty `retiredVoiceEngines[r][i]` slot. Step 2's render loop picks it up next block and continues rendering its in-flight sample / amp envelope tail; when `isFullyDrained()` returns true, the audio thread sets the cleanup flag and the next `handleAsyncUpdate` destroys it off the RT thread. Back-pressure: all 4 retired slots full → force-cut by overwriting slot 0 (matches pre-Stage-34 abrupt-cut behaviour for that one engine; system stays stable on spam-swap). The displaced slot's cleanup flag is store-released to `false` so a stale ready-flag can't trigger a wasted suspend+move on the freshly placed engine. Frozen retired state preserved by the existing design: only `voiceEngines[r]` (the active slot) gets `setActiveParams` / `trigger` / `setParams` / `loadFile`, so retired engines never see parameter writes, MIDI triggers, or APVTS sync. `oldEngine` nullness is guarded — Lite build (where `voiceEngines[r]` is always null pre-swap) skips the retire path cleanly. Effect on user-facing behaviour: load a long-sustain preset (pad, drone, long crash) while playing → click a different preset; the old sample audibly continues playing into the new rhythm's hits instead of being abruptly cut at the loop boundary. The `suspendProcessing` silence gap (~1.33 ms at 48k/64) still creates a single-block pause in the retired engine's mid-sample playback, which is Step 4's optional optimisation; in practice imperceptible on percussive material and only occasionally audible on sustained pads (matches the trade-off documented in CLAUDE.md). Built Debug + Release clean, no warnings. Test gates: Test 3.1 (long-sample swap during playback), 3.2 (spam-swap back-pressure), 3.3 (stop during retire), 3.4 (8-rhythm stress) — all require user listening verification; per the plan they're not unit-testable. Plan: [docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md](docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md). | ✅ Fixed | 484 |
| 414 | **[Stage 34 Step 2]** Retired-engine infrastructure (slots + render loop + cleanup drain, no retire-on-swap yet — that's Step 3). Added per-rhythm retired storage to PluginProcessor at [Source/PluginProcessor.h:213-225](Source/PluginProcessor.h#L213): `kMaxRetiredEngines = 4`, `retiredVoiceEngines[MaxRhythms][4]` (`std::unique_ptr<VoiceEngine>`), and parallel `retiredReadyForCleanup[MaxRhythms][4]` (`std::atomic<bool>`). C++17 `std::atomic<bool>` default ctor leaves the value indeterminate, so the PluginProcessor ctor now stores `false` into every flag unconditionally (also outside the LITE guard so Lite's handleAsyncUpdate can't ever read an indeterminate atomic). MixerEngine gained an optional `const RetiredVoices*` parameter ([Source/Audio/MixerEngine.h:10-22](Source/Audio/MixerEngine.h#L10)) carrying a flat row-major matrix of engine ptrs + cleanup flags + perSlot count — taking `.data()` of the outer std::array's first inner array yields the contiguous start of the 2D matrix that the audio thread indexes as `[r * perSlot + i]` (std::array of std::array has no inter-row padding). MixerEngine's Phase 1 voice loop ([MixerEngine.cpp:107](Source/Audio/MixerEngine.cpp#L107)) now iterates retired slots immediately after the active engine and BEFORE `applyGain(kHeadroomTrim)`, so retired tails ride the same channel fader / pan / sidechain / sends / inserts as the active engine. After each retired `process()`, `isFullyDrained()` is checked; true → flag store-released so the message thread can destroy the engine off the RT thread. ProcessorBase::processCoreBlock forwards the descriptor through ([ProcessorBase.h:30](Source/ProcessorBase.h#L30) / [.cpp:18](Source/ProcessorBase.cpp#L18)). PluginProcessor::processBlock builds the descriptor once per block from the 2D arrays' `.data()` pointers ([PluginProcessor.cpp:704-712](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L704)). handleAsyncUpdate gained a cleanup-drain block at the top that scans `retiredReadyForCleanup` for set flags; if any, suspendProcessing fences the audio thread, the engines are moved out into local unique_ptrs (audio thread sees nullptr next block), the flags are cleared (release), suspendProcessing resumes, and the local container destructs at scope exit — fully off the audio thread. Empty-fast-path: the scan returns false in zero retired engines so suspendProcessing is skipped entirely (which is every block in Step 2 — nothing populates retired slots until Step 3 — and the steady state in later steps once tails have drained). Defensive prepareToPlay loop re-prepares any populated retired engines on sample-rate / block-size changes (no-op in Step 2). Built Debug + Release clean, no warnings. Behaviour unchanged per Test 2.1 (no populator yet). Plan: [docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md](docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md). | ✅ Fixed | 483 |
| 413 | **[Stage 34 Step 1]** Foundation for seamless hot-swap with polyphonic voice tail — added `bool VoiceEngine::isFullyDrained() const noexcept` at [Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h:39](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.h#L39) / [VoiceEngine.cpp:168](Source/Audio/VoiceEngine.cpp#L168). Returns `true` only when every `SamplePlayer` voice is inactive (`playPos < 0` AND no pending trigger — `SamplePlayer::isActive()` already encapsulates both) AND `ampEnv.isActive()` is false (JUCE's idle/post-release state). `noexcept`, no side effects, no state mutation — purely an inspection that an audio-thread caller can run each block on retired engines without risking allocation or a parameter touch. No callers in this commit by design: Step 1 is foundation-only, behaviour unchanged. Step 2 wires the retired-engine slots + render loop; Step 3 wires retire-on-swap (the actual feature). Built Debug + Release clean, zero warnings. Plan: [docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md](docs/design-seamless-hotswap.md). | ✅ Fixed | 477 |

| 403 | **[Audit]** **MED** — `std::string` temporaries from `modParamValues[]` lookups eliminated. Changed the map type from `std::unordered_map<std::string, float>` to `std::unordered_map<std::string_view, float>` at [Source/PluginProcessor.h:325](Source/PluginProcessor.h#L325). All write/read sites in `processBlock` use `const char*` string literals (`modParamValues["amp.attack"]`) which have static storage — `string_view` of a literal is alloc-free and the literal's lifetime exceeds the map's. | 401 | **[Audit]** `RhythmPanel::parameterChanged` did an O(N=31) linear scan of `kEuclidSuffixes` for every parameter change. Fired on every host-automation event + every knob drag tick. | 394 | **[Audit]** UAF risk in `PluginEditor` callbacks — `processorRef.onSaveAndQuit` captured raw `[this]` but wasn't cleared in the editor dtor. | 393 | **[Audit]** `pushRhythmToAPVTS` fires APVTS broadcasts → `RhythmPanel::parameterChanged` marshals each via `juce::MessageManager::callAsync` (#354). The marshalled `refreshSuffix` calls were landing AFTER `handleAsyncUpdate`'s #386 `onRhythmHotSwapCommitted` callback had already re-bound the panels via `setRhythm()` — so each of ~30 queued per-param refreshes re-ran `setValue` on already-bound sliders. | 392 | **[Audit]** `handleAsyncUpdate` called `suspendProcessing(true/false)` INSIDE the per-rhythm loop — a MIDI program-change burst hitting multiple slots could stall the message thread for ~80 ms (8× 1–10 ms suspends back-to-back) and produce N audible dropouts. Plus `sequencer.getRhythm(r) = sw.pendingRhythm` was a copy-assign that deep-copied every modulator + control sequence vector under the suspend. Fix: restructured into three passes at [Source/PluginProcessor.cpp:951-1005](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L951): (1) collect all ready slots into a stack-allocated `std::array<int, MaxRhythms>`; (2) ONE `suspendProcessing(true)` → swap them all (with `std::move(sw.pendingRhythm)` instead of copy) → ONE `suspendProcessing(false)`; (3) post-commit APVTS push + `onRhythmHotSwapCommitted` callback for each, all under ONE `ScopedApvtsLoading` guard (so every panel's `parameterChanged` sees `apvtsLoading=true` throughout — see #391/#393). Single-swap case (the common path) pays the same suspend cost as before; multi-swap case (MIDI burst) collapses to one suspend instead of N. | ✅ Fixed | 465 |
| 391 | **[Audit]** `apvtsLoading` was a plain `bool` written on the message thread and read by `parameterChanged` listeners which can fire on the audio thread (DAW host automation, per #354). True cross-thread access with no atomic semantics. Worse, the `apvtsLoading = true; ...work...; apvtsLoading = false;` pattern at 6 sites was non-RAII — if anything in the push threw, the flag latched true and ALL subsequent parameter changes silently dropped their engine syncs. Fix: (a) declared `apvtsLoading` as `std::atomic<bool>` at [Source/PluginProcessor.h:283](Source/PluginProcessor.h#L283); (b) added `bool isApvtsLoading() const noexcept` public accessor for UI listener gating (used by #393); (c) added `mu_pp::ScopedApvtsLoading` RAII guard at [Source/PluginProcessor_Internal.h:16-32](Source/PluginProcessor_Internal.h#L16) that stores true in the ctor and false in the dtor with `memory_order_release`; (d) replaced all 6 set/clear pairs across PluginProcessor.cpp / PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp / PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp with `{ mu_pp::ScopedApvtsLoading guard(apvtsLoading); ...work... }` scope blocks. Read site at `syncRhythmParam` now uses `apvtsLoading.load(std::memory_order_acquire)`. | ✅ Fixed | 465 |
| 390 | **[Audit]** Renamed inner variable `p` → `param` in `masterVolKnob.onValueChanged` lambda at [Source/UI/SettingsOverlay.cpp:17](Source/UI/SettingsOverlay.cpp#L17). | 389 | **[Audit] HIGH** — `stageRhythmPreset` (hot-swap-while-playing) silently dropped modulator state from the loaded preset. `applyRhythmPreset` (stopped path) at [Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp:281-285](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp#L281) deserialised the preset's `Modulators` child into the target rhythm; `stageRhythmPreset` (playing path) at [Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp:32-119](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp#L32) had no equivalent block. Result: hot-swapping a rhythm preset while playing kept the previous rhythm's modulator assignments + control sequences in place, overlaid on the new rhythm's voice/pattern params. A preset designed with a specific LFO modulating cutoff arrived with the wrong LFOs. Behaviour silently differed depending on whether the user was stopped or playing at load time. Legacy `.muRhyth` files with no `Modulators` child are left alone (same opt-in policy as `applyRhythmPreset`). Sibling issue noted for follow-up: `applyDefaultRhythm` calls `applyRhythmPreset` directly regardless of play state — should also route via `stageRhythmPreset` for consistency. | ✅ Fixed | 461 |

| 387 | Settings overlay visual polish — the prior layout looked ad-hoc: 10 pt section headers, orphaned Master Vol knob at the top-left with no section, controls running to the full window width, "(host rescan required)" hint floating awkwardly, and a brittle layout where section heading Y values in `paint()` had to be hand-mirrored from `resized()` — easy to break on edits. | 386 | Hot-swap commit didn't refresh the rhythm name label (and other non-APVTS UI state) — symptom: load a new rhythm preset while playing; the sound swaps correctly but the name label still shows the old rhythm's name (e.g. "Kick" instead of "Crushed Snare"). Loading while stopped worked because `RhythmPanel`'s preset-dropdown `onChange` handler at [Source/UI/RhythmPanel.cpp:317-329](Source/UI/RhythmPanel.cpp#L317) takes the stopped branch and calls `setRhythm(currentRhythmIndex)` directly, which re-binds the name label + sample bar + sub-panels. Wired in `PluginEditor` ctor at [Source/PluginEditor.cpp:140](Source/PluginEditor.cpp#L140): if the swapped rhythm is the one currently displayed, re-call `rhythmPanel.setRhythm(r)` (re-binds name + sample + sub-panels); always repaint the sidebar (its items show name + colour); refresh `mixerOverlay` if visible (channel strips show rhythm names). | 385 | Hot-swap commit dropped the first hit of the cued rhythm — symptom: queue a rhythm B from the browser while A is playing; at the loop boundary B swaps in correctly, but B's first audible hit is one (or several) steps later than expected. Root cause: the absorb-the-current-step logic in `SequencerEngine::processBlock`'s snapshot pass at [Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.cpp:226-228](Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.cpp#L226) was written generically for "any update that sets `patternUpdated[r]=true`," intended to guard mid-step knob changes from retroactively firing the in-progress step. Hot-swap commit at [Source/PluginProcessor.cpp:968](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L968) calls the same `sequencer.updatePattern(r)`, so the snapshot pass treated the step-aligned swap identically to a mid-step knob change and absorbed B's first step. But the swap IS step-aligned (cued at the wrap, committed under `suspendProcessing`) — there's no retroactive-trigger risk to guard against. Fix: (a) added `SequencerEngine::resetStepTrackingForSwap(int r)` at [Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.h:65](Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.h#L65) which sets `lastStepIndex[r] = -1` (the same sentinel #384 introduced for cold-start). Safe to call from message thread because `handleAsyncUpdate` already holds `suspendProcessing(true)` — audio thread is paused. (b) simplified the snapshot guard from `!(effectiveStep==0 && lastStepIndex==-1)` to just `lastStepIndex[r] != -1` (the cold-start case is a strict subset — if lastStepIndex is -1 we never want to absorb regardless of effectiveStep). (c) `handleAsyncUpdate` calls `resetStepTrackingForSwap(r)` immediately after `sequencer.updatePattern(r)` inside the suspendProcessing block. Result: the new pattern fires its step at the commit `effectiveStep` (instead of the next-step-after). One residual artifact NOT addressed: the OLD pattern still fires its step 0 at the wrap, because wrap-detect happens in the same audio block where the OLD step-walk processes the wrap and triggers the old voice engine; the async commit lands a few blocks later. Eliminating that requires synchronous-on-audio-thread commit (deferred OLD-VoiceEngine destruction, message-thread cleanup queue) — invasive, not done here. So user hears: OLD-step-0 at the boundary (small unavoidable artifact), then NEW-step-K cleanly (K = effectiveStep at commit, typically 1-3 steps post-wrap depending on message-loop latency). | ✅ Fixed | 453 |
| 384 | First-play step 0 absorbed by the pattern-update snapshot — root cause of the bulk of #280's "~500 ms before first sound" complaint. Trace: `addRhythm` calls `updatePattern` which sets `patternUpdated[r]=true`. On the very first `processBlock` after launch, `SequencerEngine::processBlock`'s snapshot pass at [Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.cpp:212-228](Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.cpp#L212) saw `patternUpdated[r]=true`, snapshotted `cachedPatterns→safePatterns`, and unconditionally absorbed the current step (`lastStepIndex[r] = effectiveStep % patLen` = 0). The main step-walk then short-circuited on `stepIndex == prevStep`, so step 0 of the default rhythm never fired. First audible hit waited until step 1 — **~125 ms at 120 BPM, ~188 ms at 80 BPM, ~250 ms at 60 BPM**. Stacked on top of JUCE standalone's WASAPI device init (~200-300 ms), that's the bulk of the perceived first-play lag. The absorb was correct for mid-play knob changes (avoid retroactive hit on the step you're sitting on) and for DAW resume-from-mid-bar (same reason), but wrong for cold-start / restart-from-zero where step 0 IS the user-requested first hit. Fix: guard the absorb with `!(effectiveStep == 0 && lastStepIndex[r] == -1)`. `lastStepIndex` is filled to -1 by the ctor and only set ≥0 once a rhythm has fired, so the guard fires only on the very first block from a fresh state. Result: cold-start and standalone restart-from-zero fire step 0 inside the first audio block; mid-play knob changes and DAW mid-bar resume retain the absorb behaviour. Hot-swap commits are unaffected (`lastStepIndex` is whatever step was just playing, never -1). Tested mentally against: cold-start (fires), stop-then-start (fires, since `internalBeatPos` is reset to 0 on stop), DAW play-from-start (fires), DAW resume-from-7.5 (absorbs — no retroactive fire), knob change at step 30 (absorbs — no retroactive fire), hot-swap commit (absorbs — no off-by-one against the new pattern). | ✅ Fixed | 451 |
| 383 | Hot-swap rhythm preset (mid-play, via sidebar) committed with the wrong voice sound — symptom: queue a different rhythm from the browser while playing, it swaps at the loop boundary, but the audible filter/drive remained whatever the previous rhythm had until the user touched any knob on the new rhythm (the example was a comb-filter preset still sounding like the previous LP12 until cutoff was nudged). Root cause: `stageRhythmPreset` ([Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp:82](Source/PluginProcessor_Preset.cpp#L82)) created the staged `VoiceEngine` and called `prepareToPlay` but never pushed `newRhythm.voiceParams` to it; the swap commit in `handleAsyncUpdate` ([Source/PluginProcessor.cpp:965](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L965)) then `std::move`-d that default-constructed engine in. The follow-up `pushRhythmToAPVTS` runs under `apvtsLoading=true`, and `syncRhythmParam` ([Source/PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp:311](Source/PluginProcessor_APVTS.cpp#L311)) deliberately skips the `voiceEngines[ri]->setParams` call while that flag is set (intentional — bulk-load path batches a single sync at the end). So the swapped-in engine kept its default VoiceParams (`filterType=0` LP12, `driveChar=0` None, default ADSRs) until the next un-guarded `syncRhythmParam` from a real user knob change. Fix: in `stageRhythmPreset`, after `newVoice->prepareToPlay`, call `newVoice->setParams(newRhythm.voiceParams)` to prime `pendingParams`/`paramsDirty`. The `setParams` state survives the `std::move` (it's owned by the same VoiceEngine instance), and the first `process()` after the swap calls `applyPendingParams` → `syncFilter` → `syncEnvelopes` with the new values. `InsertProcessor` reads `activeParams` per-block so re-syncs automatically once `applyPendingParams` updates `activeParams`. | ✅ Fixed | 449 |
| 382 | Adjusting the number of steps on Ring B muted hits triggered by Ring A. Root cause: same as #360 cascade. Trace — user moves `stepsB` knob → `EuclideanPanel::stepsB.onValueChanged` calls `apvtsSet("stepsB", v)` (1st `updatePattern`), then `updateRangesB(v)` runs `hitsB.setRange(0, v, 1)`. JUCE's `Slider::setRange` clips the current `hitsB` value if it sits outside the new range and fires `onValueChange` regardless of any `dontSendNotification` the caller set elsewhere. That spurious callback re-enters `apvtsSet("hitsB", clipped)` → 2nd `updatePattern`. Each `updatePattern` sets `patternUpdated[r]=true`; the next `SequencerEngine::processBlock` snapshots the new pattern AND resets `lastStepIndex[r] = effectiveStep % patLen`. The main step-walk then short-circuits on `if (stepIndex == prevStep) continue;` — the current step's hit is intentionally absorbed (per "Absorb the current step so we don't retroactively fire a hit", [SequencerEngine.cpp:223](Source/Sequencer/SequencerEngine.cpp#L223)). While the user drags the knob, this fires every block across both rhythms (combined pattern uses LCM(A,B) so B-changes recompute A's contribution too), so every block in flight skips its hit → audible muting of A. Fix lives in [KnobWithLabel](Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.cpp) — see #360. | ✅ Fixed | 436 |
| 381 | `mu-clid_installer` CMake target only depended on `mu-clid` (the JUCE shared-lib target), not on the format outputs `mu-clid_VST3`/`mu-clid_CLAP`/`mu-clid_Standalone`. MSBuild ran the installer in parallel with the Standalone build and the Inno Setup script failed: "Source file `Release\Standalone\mu-Clid.exe` does not exist". Surfaced only on clean builds — incremental builds masked it because Standalone always existed from a prior build. Same latent issue for `mu-clid-lite_installer`. | 360 | **[Audit]** [Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.cpp:15-22](Source/UI/Components/KnobWithLabel.cpp#L15) — when `setRange()` clips the slider's current value to the new range, JUCE fires `onValueChange` regardless of any prior `dontSendNotification` the caller had set. `EuclideanPanel::updateRangesA/B/C` triggered this every time the user changed steps, cascading through `apvtsSet` → APVTS broadcast → audio-thread `updatePattern` and the message-thread `RhythmPanel::parameterChanged` reload. | 359 | **[Audit]** `NudgeInput::showEditor` heap-allocated a `juce::TextEditor` and wired three async lambdas (`onReturnKey`/`onFocusLost`/`onEscapeKey`) that captured raw `this` without `Component::SafePointer<NudgeInput>`. | 358 | **[Audit]** `ReverbSlot::setParam` / `updateReverb` wrote `impl->reverb.roomMs`/`rt20`/`early`/`highDampRate`/`lowDampRate`/`detune`/`lowCutHz`/`highCutHz` directly from the message thread while `processReturn` ran `impl->reverb.process()` concurrently on the audio thread — undefined per typical embedded reverb single-threaded-access assumptions. | 357 | **[Audit]** `voiceEngines[r]->setActiveParams(modParams)` ran every block per rhythm at [PluginProcessor.cpp:904](Source/PluginProcessor.cpp#L904) regardless of whether the modulation pass actually executed. For an unmodulated rhythm `modParams ≡ rhythm.voiceParams ≡ activeParams` (already kept in sync by `VoiceEngine::applyPendingParams`'s dirty-flag path), so each call was pure waste — `syncEnvelopes()` + `syncFilter()` re-running on identical state. | 356 | **[Audit]** `RhythmPanel::commitNameFromLabel` wrote `proc.getRhythm(idx).name = newName.toStdString();` directly from the message thread, bypassing all serialisation with audio-thread state. Investigation found no audio-thread reader of `rhythm.name` today (state save/load, UI display, and MixerOverlay labels are all message-thread; MidiOutputEngine doesn't reference name), so the audit's "MIDI PC matcher" concern was speculative. Still applied a defensive fix: routed the write through new `PluginProcessor::renameRhythm(int, juce::String)` which takes `rhythmsLock` — the project's canonical "message thread mutates Rhythm" serialiser, paired with the audio thread's `ScopedTryLock(rhythmsLock)` in `processBlock`. Stays correct if a future audio-path consumer (e.g. MIDI program-change preset matcher) reads name. No UI-thread modLock spin. | ✅ Fixed | 440 |
| 355 | **[Audit]** `RhythmPanel::confirmReset` spun on `r.modLock.compare_exchange_weak` on the UI thread. If the audio thread was preempted while holding `modLock` (OS scheduler / DAW low-priority audio mode) the UI froze. Worse, after acquire, `r = Rhythm{}` triggered `std::vector` destructors in `modulationMatrix`/`controlSequences` while a concurrent in-flight `modulationMatrix.process()` may already have cached references to the old assignments — acquire/release on `modLock` doesn't save you once `process()` is already past the try-lock. Fix: extracted the reset into new `PluginProcessor::resetRhythm(int)` using the same `suspendProcessing(true)` + `ScopedLock(rhythmsLock)` pattern already used by `removeRhythm` / `swapRhythmSlots`. `suspendProcessing` halts new audio-thread entries; `rhythmsLock` waits for the in-flight `processBlock`'s `ScopedTryLock` to release. UI-thread spin gone; safe atomic swap of the Rhythm struct. | ✅ Fixed | 440 |
| 354 | **[Audit]** `RhythmPanel::parameterChanged` was invoked by JUCE on whatever thread called `setValueNotifyingHost` — in some DAWs that's the audio thread for host automation — and the handler called `euclidPanel.loadFromRhythm()` / `voiceSection.loadFromRhythm()` which mutate `juce::Slider` state. Slider ops are not audio-thread-safe → potential crash / UB. Fix: handler now captures a `Component::SafePointer<RhythmPanel>` + the suffix, then either runs inline if already on the message thread or marshals via `juce::MessageManager::callAsync`. SafePointer guards against panel teardown between the audio-thread enqueue and the message-thread dispatch (preset reload / rhythm switch). | ✅ Fixed | 437 |
| 353 | **[Audit]** Every rhythm parameter change reset the *entire* euclidean panel (21 knobs + 9 segment controls) or voice section (28+ knobs) via `loadFromRhythm` — one knob touch ≡ whole panel rewrite, multiplied by every parameterChanged event in the cascade. Fix: added `EuclideanPanel::refreshSuffix(suffix)` and `VoiceSection::refreshSuffix(suffix)`, each an if/else chain mapping a single APVTS suffix to the one knob/segment that owns it. `RhythmPanel::parameterChanged` (now message-thread-marshalled per [[#354]]) calls `refreshSuffix` instead of `loadFromRhythm`. Insert-knob suffixes (`drvDrv`/`drvOut`/`drvDit`/`drvTon`/`drvBits`/`drvRate`/`eqMidGain`) re-run `configureInsertAlgorithm` because the layout depends on `driveChar` — still cheaper than a full reload. `loadFromRhythm` retained for `setRhythm`/preset-load paths that genuinely need a full refresh. | ✅ Fixed | 437 |
| 352 | **[Audit]** `MixerOverlay` registered an APVTS listener for *every* parameter in the entire tree (hundreds across all rhythms / voices / mods) and set `apvtsDirty=true` on any change. Each dirty-flag flush called `loadFromAPVTS` which rebuilds every mixer channel strip — wasted work on every rhythm/euclid/voice/mod knob change, and a feedback-storm risk via the universal listener. Fix: added `isMixerRelevantParam(id)` helper that recognises only mixer-relevant prefixes — `ch{N}_*` rhythm channels, `ret_eff_*`/`ret_dly_*`/`ret_rev_*` returns, `mstr_*`/`mst_ins*` master + inserts, `eff_*`/`dly_*`/`rev_*`/`echo_*` FX algorithm + params. Constructor + destructor parameter-listener loops filter through this predicate. Verified the prefix list against the actual `addParameter` registrations in `PluginProcessor.cpp` — no mixer-affecting IDs missed. Rhythm/euclid/voice/mod knob movements no longer trigger spurious mixer reloads. | ✅ Fixed | 444 |
| 351 | **[Audit]** Apparent policy contradiction between `.claude/commands/bug.md`/`update.md` ("never use suffix notation") and the MEMORY.md index entry for `feedback_backlog_single_issue.md` ("MANDATORY: split combined rows using suffix notation #178a/b"). Investigation: the actual `feedback_backlog_single_issue.md` body already says **"Never use suffix notation"** — only the one-line index summary in MEMORY.md was wrong. Fix: corrected the MEMORY.md index line to "split into next sequential whole numbers — NEVER use suffix notation". Bug.md / update.md unchanged (already correct). | ✅ Fixed | 433 |
| 350 | **[Audit]** [backlog.md](backlog.md) Fixed section ordering broken at the top: rows appeared as `338, 337, 336, 348, 347, 346, 345, 344, 343, 342…`. | 349 | **[Audit] URGENT** — `.claude/settings.json` PostToolUse hook was copying **Debug** Standalone/VST3/CLAP to `TDP/Windows/` on every `cmake --build`, running AFTER CMake's Release deploy and overwriting it. Testers were receiving Debug builds for an unknown period. Fix: changed the three Copy-Item paths from `\\Debug\\` to `\\Release\\` so the hook now mirrors CMake's deploy semantics. | 348 | Euclid modulation scales too aggressive (sibling of #336) — fixed scales of 16 (hits / rotate / insSt) covered the full slider range at typical steps=16, so any moderate depth saturated the pattern. Halved scales: hits/rotate/insSt 16→8, prePad/postPad 12→6, insLen 8→4. Same proportions, half the magnitude — user dials depth higher to get the old feel. | ✅ Fixed | 427 |
| 347 | Return solo doesn't suppress rhythm dry passthrough (sibling of #337) — when a return channel (Effect/Delay/Reverb) was soloed, the user heard the soloed return's wet PLUS the rhythm channels' dry going to master, because the rhythm-channel mute logic only considered rhythm-channel solo state. Fix: rhythm channels now skip the addFrom to master (but still feed FX sends, so the soloed return has source material) when any return is soloed. Hard-mute path (mute || rhythm-solo-and-not-this) unchanged. | ✅ Fixed | 427 |
| 346 | Runtime-verify #345 fix — confirmed in standalone: removing the last `euclid.*` modulation assignment mid-play causes the pattern to snap back to base within one buffer. Stage A/B/C wiring + #345 polish work as designed. | ✅ Fixed | 426 |
| 345 | Removing all euclid pattern modulation assignments while playing left a stale modulated pattern (sibling of #336) — root cause was the `if (!getAssignments().empty())` guard in `PluginProcessor::processBlock`'s modulation loop, which skipped the `lastEuclidOverrides[r]` write-back when the matrix became empty. Fix: drop the guard so the modulation pass always runs (ModulationMatrix::process() already returns early when assignments is empty — cost is ~40 hash writes per rhythm). lastEuclidOverrides now re-converges to base values one block after assignment removal; Stage B change-detection then recomputes the safe pattern back to base. Cleaner than UI-side `updatePattern()` plumbing because it works for every removal path (state restore, programmatic removal, dropdown-change-source). | ✅ Fixed | 425 |

| 295 | Sidebar drag-reorder — sidechain source indices not re-translated (sibling of #190). | 291 | Filter cutoff modulation now multiplicative in octaves, not additive in Hz (sibling of #216/#289/#290). `ModulationMatrix::depthScaleFor("filter.cutoff")` and `depthScaleFor("insert.lpf")` changed from 8000 (Hz) to 48 (semitones, =±4 octaves) — matching `filterEnvDepth`. New `isLogHzDest()` helper drives the apply step: `dst *= 2^(amount / 12.0f)` for Hz destinations, additive for everything else. Same depth now sweeps the same number of octaves whether the base cutoff is 100 Hz or 10 kHz. **Preset-feel change** for any existing patch using cutoff modulation, but no API/format break. Code references this as `// #216 #4` and now should be read as `// #291`. | ✅ Fixed | 335 |

| 288 | Legacy host-state migration for the #217/#286/#287 ADSR unit flip. Completes the cherry-pick recovery batch. Without this, a Bitwig (or any DAW) session saved before #217/#286/#287 would reload with the old 0..100 attack/decay/release values clamped to the new 0..10 s max — a previously-tuned 30/100 (0.9s) attack would become a 10s attack (or 30s if no clamp). Fix: new `kCurrentStateFormatVersion = 2` constant at the top of `PluginProcessor.cpp`. `populateStateTree` writes `formatVersion` as a property on the state root. New `migrateLegacyHostState(ValueTree&)` helper iterates `<PARAM>` children, identifies ADSR-time IDs (`r{N}_(aEnvAtk\|Dec\|Rel\|fEnvAtk\|Dec\|Rel\|pEnvAtk\|Dec\|Rel)`), multiplies their value by 0.03 (the old display→seconds factor) and clamps to 0..10. Special case for `aEnvRel`: old value >= 100 (End-mode sentinel) maps to new value 10 (new End-mode sentinel) so "play to natural end" patches round-trip correctly. The migration helper is called from `restoreStateFromTree` on a `state.createCopy()` so the original tree is untouched. Final step writes `formatVersion = 2` so re-loading a migrated state is a no-op. `.muclid` / `.muRhyth` preset files are out of scope (no presets saved yet); follow-up if needed once presets exist. | ✅ Fixed | 345 |
| 287 | Pitch envelope time params (`pEnvAtk` / `pEnvDec` / `pEnvRel`) migrated from `0..100` linear → `0..10 seconds` with skew 0.3 — completes the ADSR unit-flip trio after #217 (amp) and #286 (filter). APVTS layout for the three params switched from `addF(..., 0, 100, …)` to `addAdsrT(...)` so DAW automation lanes show "X ms" / "X.XX s" with knob centre at ~100–200 ms. `applyRhythmSuffix` writes seconds directly via `juce::jmax(0.001f, v)` instead of `adsrTime(v)`; `pushRhythmToAPVTS` writes seconds directly (no `* (100/3)`). VoiceSection: pitchAtk/Dec/Rel ranges flipped to `(0, 10, 0.001)` with `setSkewFactor(0.3)`; pitch knobs merged into the unified seconds-domain formatter loop alongside amp + filter (legacy `formatAdsrTime` / `parseAdsrTime` helpers now unused but retained for one release as a safety net); `loadFromRhythm` strips the `* (100/3)` conversion. Default knob values rounded at the boundary: 0.0 → 0.0 s (was 0/100), 1.0 → 0.03 s (was 1/100 = ~30 ms with old mapping). Sustain stays 0..100 %. No pitch envelope destinations exist in the modulation system, so no snapshot/apply round-trip changes needed (only `pitch.envDepth` is modulatable, which is already in semitones). | 285 | Mixer Effect FX dropdown listener-skip on unchanged value (HIGH, user-visible — sibling of #242). | 281 | Accent ring visual jumps back to start when combined A+B pattern wraps — `rotAngleC` was computed as `(currentStep % stepsC)` where `currentStep = effectiveStep % patLen`. | 280 | First-play audio delay — standalone played for ~500 ms before any sound was heard on the very first play after launch. Root cause was a combination of (a) JUCE standalone's WASAPI device init (~200-300 ms — inherent to the JUCE wrapper, not our code) and (b) the sequencer absorbing step 0 of the default rhythm on the very first `processBlock`, pushing the first audible hit to step 1 (~125-250 ms depending on BPM). The audible component is fully addressed by [[#384]]: cold-start and standalone restart-from-zero now fire step 0 inside the first audio block. The residual WASAPI device-init delay is JUCE-side and out of scope. | ✅ Fixed | 451 |

| 254 | RhythmCircle hit pulse / hub flash were dim and easy to miss (sibling of #252, #253). | 253 | RhythmCircle hits visually fired at 9 o'clock instead of 12 o'clock (sibling of #252). Root cause: `drawRing` and the arc-pulse renderer both used `startOff = -juce::MathConstants<float>::halfPi - rotOff` — that −halfPi was written as if standard math conventions applied (0 = east, π/2 = north), but JUCE's `Path::addCentredArc` measures angles from the TOP (12 o'clock) and increases clockwise. So an angle of −π/2 actually placed step 0 at 9 o'clock (west), and the rotating ring made hits flash at the 9 o'clock anchor. Fix: drop the −halfPi from both `startOff` in `drawRing` and `startA` in the pulse render path so step 0 sits at angle 0 (= 12 o'clock) when rotOff/rotAngleA is 0. Loop-point divider line updated to use the addCentredArc convention (`x = cx + r·sin(angle)`, `y = cy − r·cos(angle)`) instead of standard `cos`/`sin` so the divider and the segment boundaries now share one anchor. | ✅ Fixed | 349 |
| 252 | Sidebar mini-circle pattern stuck on the snapshot taken at construction — edits to hits/rotation/steps/insert/pad in the main `EuclideanPanel` updated the main `RhythmCircle` (via `RhythmPanel::refreshCircle`) but never propagated to the sidebar item, so the two circles diverged. Root cause: `SidebarItem::setRhythm` calls `miniCircle.setPatterns(...)` once and the only refresh path was `RhythmSidebar::refreshItems()` (rebuilds all items), which the sidebar timer only triggers when `proc.getNumRhythms() != items.size()` (per #183). Pattern changes within an existing rhythm slot weren't a trigger. Fix: `SidebarItem::timerCallback` (30 Hz) now re-reads `rhythm->genA/B/C.getStepTypes()` and compares against a cached snapshot; only re-pushes to the mini-circle on actual content change so we don't repaint 30×/s. | 251 | Preset dropdown not sorted alphabetically (sibling of #250). `TransportBar::populatePresetDropdown` iterated `dir.findChildFiles(...)` directly — JUCE's filesystem order is platform/FS-dependent (alphabetical on NTFS but not guaranteed elsewhere, mtime on some filesystems), so dropdown order was unpredictable. | 250 | Standalone app loads previous session state on startup instead of the user's saved `_default.muclid`. | 249 | Master 3-Band EQ insert knobs visually off-centre at 0 dB. User screenshot showed Low/Mid/High all reading "+0.0 dB" but with the High pointer pulled noticeably right of centre and Mid slightly off. Root cause: `setSkewFactor` is sticky on a JUCE `Slider` — when switching algorithms inside the master insert strip, the prior algorithm's log skew (e.g. Compressor's `setSkewFactorFromMidPoint(200)` on insTone, Bitcrusher's `setSkewFactorFromMidPoint(2190)` on insOutput, Tape Sat's `setSkewFactorFromMidPoint(2000)` on insTone) carried over into the ±18 dB EQ knobs. With skew ≈ 0.3 over range -18..+18, the proportional centre (value 0 = position 0.5) renders at `0.5^0.3 ≈ 0.81` — 81% of travel, well past the visual middle. Fix: explicit `getSlider().setSkewFactor(1.0)` on all three insDrive/insOutput/insTone knobs at the top of case 6, restoring linear mapping so 0 dB renders dead-centre. The per-rhythm EQ already does this for driveTone (line 601) but the master path didn't. | ✅ Fixed | 347 |
| 248 | 3-Band EQ master insert: Mid Freq knob was missing — master EQ had only Low / Mid gain / High while the per-rhythm EQ exposes all four controls (Low / Mid gain / Mid Hz / High). | 247 | Reverb FX row controls now display percentage values (sibling family — applies to all unitless 0..1 FXParamDef entries). `FXRow::rebuildKnobs` extended with three new format branches: `units == "%"` → "X %"; `units == "ms"` → "X ms" / "X.XX s" rolls over at 1000 ms; `minVal == 0 && maxVal == 1` (unitless) → "X %" treating the 0..1 stored value as a percentage. Effect row Hz formatter (existing) preserved. APVTS storage stays 0..1 — no preset-compat break, formatter only. | ✅ Fixed | 346 |
| 246 | GR (gain reduction) meter on the Output knob for Compressor and Limiter inserts. When the Compressor (char=7) or Limiter (char=8) algorithm is active, an orange arc sweeps anti-clockwise from the 5 o'clock position over the Output knob's ring, proportional to current GR (1.0 ≡ 24 dB). `InsertProcessor` gained a `juce::Atomic<float> grReduction` member, reset to 0 at the start of every block and written to the peak per-block GR value in cases 7/8. `KnobWithLabel` now inherits `juce::Timer` privately and adds `setGRSource(const juce::Atomic<float>*)` — when a source is set the knob polls at 30 Hz (instant attack / 0.85-per-frame release ballistics) and repaints. The orange arc is drawn in `paintOverChildren` inside the existing modulation-overlay path. `VoiceEngine::insertProc` moved from private to public so `VoiceSection` can wire the GR source for per-rhythm inserts. `MixerChannel` wires the master insert's GR source from `masterInsertProc->mixerEngine.masterInsert.grReduction`. All non-comp/limiter algorithm paths call `setGRSource(nullptr)` on `insOutput` / `driveOutput` so the timer stops and the arc disappears. | ✅ Fixed | 357 |
| 245 | Soft Clip / Hard Clip / Fold insert Drive knob now displays dB instead of raw 0..100. The internal pre-gain formula is `preGain = pow(10, driveDrive/100 × 2)`, so the 0..100 slider linearly maps to 0..40 dB of input gain. Knob now shows e.g. "12.0 dB" at slider value 30. Applied to both `VoiceSection` (per-rhythm insert) and `MixerChannel` (master insert) `configureInsertAlgorithm` cases 1/2/3. Clipper (case 5) uses a different formula (drvDrive as threshold fraction) and keeps raw display — covered by a follow-up. | 244 | 3-Band EQ master-insert Mid knob moved to the middle of the 3-knob column (sibling of #284). `MixerChannel::configureInsertAlgorithm` case 6 slot mapping changed from `insDrive=Low / insOutput=High / insTone=Mid` to `insDrive=Low / insOutput=Mid / insTone=High` so the visual order matches the spectral order. | 243 | Master-channel insert algorithm switches but Drive/Output/Tone knobs don't affect the sound (HIGH, user-visible). Reproduce: open standalone, mixer overlay → master channel insert → pick any algorithm (Soft Clip, Bitcrusher, etc.) → turn the Drive knob → no audible change. Root cause in `MixerChannel::configureInsertAlgorithm`: the `setParam` lambda captures the `proc` *parameter*. When the method is re-invoked from `loadFromAPVTS` (which fires every time **any** APVTS parameter changes — and the user touching the algorithm dropdown causes mst_insChar to change, which causes `loadFromAPVTS` to fire), the call passes `proc=nullptr` (to deliberately suppress the algo write-back and avoid feedback loops). The dropdown-write-back guard worked correctly — but the same nullptr propagated into the knob `onValueChanged` lambdas that the method *also* rebinds inside each algorithm case (`insDrive.onValueChanged = [setParam](double v) { setParam("mst_insDrv", v); }`). After any APVTS change, the lambdas were bound to a `setParam` whose `proc` was null, so future user knob movements silently no-op'd: no APVTS write → `parameterChanged` never fires → `masterInsertParams.driveDrive` stays at 0 → InsertProcessor's pre-gain stays at 1 (no audible saturation). A secondary symptom is that the initial knob values were read from `VoiceParams{}` (defaults) when proc was null instead of the live `mixerEngine.masterInsertParams`. Fix: new `PluginProcessor* masterInsertProc` member on `MixerChannel`, captured in `bindMaster`. `configureInsertAlgorithm`'s knob-callback `setParam` lambda now captures `masterInsertProc` instead of the parameter `proc`, so callbacks stay live across reload cycles. The `ip` source for the initial knob values now reads from `masterInsertProc->mixerEngine.masterInsertParams`, so reload shows the engine's current values rather than defaults. The function parameter `proc` retains its existing role — non-null guards the explicit `setParam("mst_insChar", charId)` write-back at the end of each case so feedback loops from loadFromAPVTS are still avoided. | ✅ Fixed | 343 |
| 242 | Mixer Effect FX engine/APVTS divergence on state restore (HIGH, user-visible — sibling of #285). `syncFXParam` for `eff_algo` / `rev_algo` had `if (!apvtsLoading) eff.setAlgorithm(...)` — during host-state restore (`apvtsLoading=true`), the algorithm change to APVTS was applied but the engine's `setAlgorithm` was skipped. Nothing re-synced the engine after the load completed, so APVTS held the restored value (e.g. 2 = Phaser) while the engine sat at default (0 = Chorus). Fix: removed the `if (!apvtsLoading)` guards on `eff_algo` and `rev_algo` in `syncFXParam` — `setAlgorithm` rebuild is cheap (one `make_unique` + `prepareInner`), fine to run during state restore. See #285 for the related listener-skip half. | ✅ Fixed | 342 |
| 241 | Transport-bar preset dropdown always displays `<unnamed preset>` placeholder, never the currently-loaded preset's name. Root cause in `TransportBar.cpp` `presetDropdown.onChange`: after firing `onPresetSelected(file)` the handler explicitly reset `presetDropdown.setSelectedId(0, false)` — designed to allow re-selecting the same item to trigger a reload, but it left the dropdown showing the placeholder text immediately after every load. Fix: (1) removed the `setSelectedId(0, false)` reset in `onChange` so the dropdown keeps the selected item visible after load; (2) new public `TransportBar::setLoadedPreset(const juce::File&)` method that finds the matching item by full path and selects it (or reverts to placeholder when the file is invalid / not in the dropdown list — e.g. preset saved outside the user Presets dir); (3) `PluginEditor` calls `transportBar.setLoadedPreset(f)` from all three external load paths — `onPresetSelected`, `presetBrowser.onLoadPreset`, and the `saveDialog.onSave` callback (after `refreshPresets()` repopulates so the just-saved item is in the list). Save path mirrors `savePreset`'s filename sanitisation (`\/:\|*?<>"` → `_`, empty → "Preset") to compute the just-saved file path. Host-state restore path (`setStateInformation` / `restoreStateFromTree`) does not set a loaded preset — the placeholder remains correct in that case since the host state isn't a file. | ✅ Fixed | 340 |
| 240 | Rhythms silent after `preset A → preset B → preset A` cycle (HIGH). Reproduce: in Bitwig (or any host), load a multi-rhythm preset, hit play, switch to a single-rhythm preset, then switch back to the original — slots beyond #0 visually reload but produce no audio. Root cause: `sequencer.setNumRhythms()` shrinks the active rhythm count by destroying `Rhythm` objects on slots ≥ n, then growing back to the original count re-creates those slots with **default** `Rhythm` fields (`HitGenerator::hits = 0`, default `voiceParams`). When the preset reloads identical APVTS values onto those re-defaulted slots, JUCE's `setValueNotifyingHost` skips the listener callback because the value is unchanged — so `parameterChanged → syncRhythmParam → applyRhythmSuffix` never fires, leaving `r.voiceParams` and `r.genA.hits` at defaults: silent slot. Fix: new private `PluginProcessor::forceSyncRhythmFromAPVTS(int ri)` that iterates every `kRhythmSuffixes` entry and calls `applyRhythmSuffix` directly with the current `apvts.getRawParameterValue()->load()`, bypassing JUCE's unchanged-value skip; internally invokes `sequencer.updatePattern(ri)` when patternDirty and `voiceEngines[ri]->setParams(r.voiceParams)`. Wired into all three preset-load paths: `restoreStateFromTree` (host APVTS state), `loadPreset` (.muclid full presets), `applyRhythmPreset` (.muRhyth single-rhythm presets) — each replacing or augmenting the existing `updatePattern + setParams` pair. Pre-existing bug latent since the `setNumRhythms`-destroys-on-shrink behaviour was introduced; exposed by today's preset-cycle testing. | ✅ Fixed | 339 |
| 239 | Modulator Loop / Step multiplier label rendered as garbled glyphs ("Ä□ 4" instead of "× 4"). | 237 | Modulator state persistence (HIGH). Schema: `<Modulators rhythmIdx="N">` with `<Seq id="csN" mode polarity loopNV loopMod loopMult stepNV stepMod stepMult>` children carrying `<Step v>` and `<Point x y bez hx hy>` elements, plus `<Asgn id src dest depth curve>` entries. | 236 | `ModMatrixPanel` ModLock wrapping (HIGH). | 235 | `swapRhythms` now holds `rhythmsLock` around the data swap (MEDIUM). `PluginProcessor::swapRhythms` previously relied on `suspendProcessing(true)` alone — but per `PluginProcessor.h:266` that only sets a flag and does NOT block the in-flight `processBlock` callback. Wrapped the entire swap mutation block (`sequencer.swapRhythmSlots`, voice/midi `std::swap`, sidechain re-translation, mixer-channel `std::swap`, env resets) in `{ const juce::ScopedLock sl(rhythmsLock); … }`. | 234 | Audio-thread allocation in pattern snapshot eliminated (MEDIUM). `SequencerEngine` ctor now calls `safePatterns[i].reserve(256)` and `safeCPatterns[i].reserve(256)` for all 8 slots (256 = the `resetSteps` cap and `getCombinedPattern`'s LCM clamp). The snapshot copy in `processBlock` switched from `=` copy-assignment (which can allocate when capacity < source size) to `assign(begin, end)` which reuses the existing storage — guaranteed no-alloc on the audio thread for any pattern size ≤ 256 steps. | ✅ Fixed | 331 |
| 233 | Negative `beatPos` no longer produces OOB pattern indexing (MEDIUM). `SequencerEngine::processBlock` clamps `globalStep = std::max(0, static_cast<int>(beatPosition / StepLengthBeats))` so hosts emitting negative ppq (pre-roll, REW-past-zero, transport jumps) can't drive `effectiveStep` negative — eliminates the signed-int `%` UB that previously made `pattern[stepIndex]` index a negative offset. | ✅ Fixed | 332 |
| 232 | Step-skip on very large blocks fixed (MEDIUM). `SequencerEngine::processBlock` now walks every step crossed between `lastStepIndex[r]` (exclusive) and `stepIndex` (inclusive), so a single huge block (offline render, unusual hosts up to 8192-sample blocks) catches all intermediate hits instead of dropping them silently. Modular forward walk capped at `patLen` to avoid infinite loops on degenerate jumps. `firedMask` stays one bit per rhythm per block (per audit recommendation); `accentMask` reflects the last hit's accent state from `safeCPatterns`. Rhythm-loop-wrap detection (`rhythmLoopWrapMask`) fires whenever the walk reaches step 0. First-call path (`prevStep < 0`) preserved: check current step directly, no back-walk. | ✅ Fixed | 332 |
| 231 | `lastEffectiveStep` reset on master-loop change and transport stop→start (MEDIUM). `SequencerEngine::setMasterLoopSteps` now resets `lastEffectiveStep = -1` so a mid-playback loop-length change can't emit a false `masterLoopWrapped` event from the stale value. New `SequencerEngine::resetWrapDetector()` public method; `PluginProcessor::processBlock` detects the `playing` false→true edge (comparing against `sequencerPlaying.get()` from the previous block) and calls it, so a transport stop→start can't trigger a false wrap either. False wraps previously gated hot-swap commits, so this also stops premature staged-swap commits. | ✅ Fixed | 331 |
| 230 | `internalBeatPos` and `internalPlaying` are now `std::atomic<>` (MEDIUM). Previously plain `double` / `bool` written by the audio thread (inside `processBlock`) and read+cleared by the UI thread (`isInternalPlaying`, `toggleInternalPlay`) — racy by the C++ memory model. Switched to `std::atomic<double> internalBeatPos` and `std::atomic<bool> internalPlaying`; all read/write call sites updated to use `.load(std::memory_order_relaxed)` / `.store(…, std::memory_order_relaxed)`. No other memory is published through them so relaxed ordering is sufficient. `internalBpm` stays plain — message-thread only. | ✅ Fixed | 331 |

| 225 | Cubic Bézier evaluator `handleX` documented as deliberately unused (LOW). `ControlSequence::CurvePoint::handleX` retained in the struct for forward-compat — comment added to the struct definition flagging that `evaluateSmooth` is intentionally 1-D in y-over-chord (a true 2-D evaluator complicates the playhead-vs-time mapping and is not free), so anyone authoring presets externally should not expect horizontal-handle effects. | ✅ Fixed | 330 |
| 224 | Source-side curve on assignments — implemented Bitwig-style per-assignment bipolar curve knob. New `curve` field on `ModulationAssignment` (range −100..+100, default 0). `ModulationMatrix::process` applies a sign-preserving power bend to each source value before depth scaling: `k = 2^(curve/100)`, `srcVal = sign(srcVal) · \|srcVal/100\|^k · 100`. So curve=0 → linear (k=1), curve=+100 → exponential (k=2, compress low/expand high), curve=−100 → logarithmic (k=0.5, expand low/compress high). New `ModulationMatrix::setCurve(id, value)` API. UI: both `ModulatorEditor::AssignmentRow` and `ModMatrixPanel::MatrixRow` gain a compact rotary curve slider after the depth slider, with double-click-to-zero. `onCurveChange` callback wired into both panels' lock/unlock paths; curve preserved across destination changes. Skipped at curve=0 (one float compare) so unused assignments pay no cost. | ✅ Fixed | 334 |

| 222 | Cubic Bézier evaluation implemented in `ControlSequence::evaluateSmooth`. When neither endpoint has a handle, the segment falls back to the existing linear interpolation, so current presets (no handle-bearing points saved) render identically. | 192 | Comb- filter — new negative-feedback variant of the existing Comb. Type code 15 in `MultiModeFilter`: `y[n] = x[n] − g·y[n−D]`, producing resonant peaks at odd half-multiples of `f0 = sr/D` (f0/2, 3f0/2, 5f0/2…), one octave below the equivalent Comb+ and with the characteristic Karplus-Strong "plucked-string" character. Implementation reuses the existing `combBuffer[ch]` + `combWritePos[ch]` state (only one comb sign is active at a time); the dispatch in `MultiModeFilter::process` merges types 8 and 15 and flips the feedback gain sign for type 15. `fltType` APVTS int range extended 0–14 → 0–15; the `jlimit` guard in `parameterChanged` and the comment on `VoiceParams::filterType` updated to match. `VoiceSection` dropdown gains a "Comb −" item placed next to the renamed "Comb +" entry. | ✅ Fixed | 328 |
| 191 | Tempo-synced FX (Delay slot + Echo) used the standalone `internalBpm` regardless of whether the plugin was running standalone or in a DAW — so a host running at any tempo other than 120 produced wrong delay times (the dotted-8th complaint was the visible symptom). Fix in `PluginProcessor::processBlock` just before `fxChain.setHostBpm()`: capture an `effectiveBpm` that prefers `getPlayHead()->getPosition()->getBpm()` when the host provides it, falls back to `midiClockBpmEst.get()` when MIDI clock sync is locked in standalone, and uses `internalBpm` only as a last resort. The sync math itself (`beatMs * 4 / denom × 1.5` for dotted) was already correct — only the BPM input was wrong. | ✅ Fixed | 324 |
| 190 | Sidebar drag-reorder — `pushMixerChannelToAPVTS` missing five suffixes (sibling of #295). | 189 | Reverb knobs (and effect-row knobs, though less noticeable) would register one mouse drag step then go dead. Root cause in `FXRow::setSelectedAlgorithm`: the method called `rebuildKnobs(currentAlgorithm)` unconditionally, destroying every slider component. `MixerOverlay::loadFromAPVTS` calls `setSelectedAlgorithm(currentAlgo, ...)` on every APVTS refresh tick (30 Hz, triggered when ANY parameter changes — including the very knob the user is dragging), so the user's first drag fired `parameterChanged` → `apvtsDirty` → next tick → knobs rebuilt mid-drag → mouse capture lost on the destroyed slider, subsequent mouseMove events went nowhere. Fix: make `setSelectedAlgorithm` idempotent — early-return when the algorithm index hasn't actually changed, so the typical loadFromAPVTS refresh path becomes a no-op for the row whose algorithm is stable. | ✅ Fixed | 324 |
| 188 | Mixer GR meter — permanent grey vertical strip visible on every rhythm channel even when no sidechain ducking is active (sibling of #296/#297). `GRMeter::paint` unconditionally drew its dark `0xff111111` slot background + black border before the fill, so an empty meter still rendered as a thin dark rectangle next to the VU meter — visually indistinguishable from a stuck low-value fill. Fixed by early-returning from `paint` when `displayGR <= 0.005f` (the existing visibility threshold), so the meter is completely invisible until ducking actually occurs. | ✅ Fixed | 321 |
| 187 | Lite-build C4702 unreachable-code warning cluster (~80 warnings) eliminated. `PluginProcessor::processBlock` previously gated Lite-only logic with `#if MUCLID_LITE_BUILD { … return; } #endif` followed by full-mode code. In Lite builds the compiler saw the unconditional `return;` inside the always-taken `#if` block and flagged every line of full-mode code (lines 461–765) as unreachable. Refactored to `#if MUCLID_LITE_BUILD … #else … #endif` so only one path is compiled per build target. Three edits: (1) removed the inner `{` after the `#if` and the matching `} // end MUCLID_LITE_BUILD scope` + `return;`; (2) replaced the inner `#endif` with `#else`; (3) added a new `#endif` immediately before `processBlock`'s closing `}`. Behaviour bit-identical for both targets — both branches are mutually exclusive (no shared cleanup; the Lite block already returned naturally). Verified by force-rebuilding `PluginProcessor.cpp` in both targets (`mu-clid` and `mu-clid-lite`) at both Debug and Release configs — zero project warnings. Whole project now compiles warning-free apart from the JUCE `Font(float)` C4996 deprecations explicitly deferred per CLAUDE.md. | ✅ Fixed | 315 |
| 186 | Build-warning cleanup — `RhythmCircle` unused `sA` / `sB` locals (sibling of #298). `RhythmCircle.cpp:202–203` C4189 — `sA` and `sB` locals were initialised from `playState->stepsA/stepsB` but never read; ring step indices are derived from `combinedStep % patternA.size()` instead (avoids a race between pattern update and atomic). Both unused variables removed; the surrounding comment rewritten to explain the pattern-size approach. | ✅ Fixed | 311 |
| 185 | `MultiModeFilter` notch dry-subtract loops optimised (sibling of #299). The inefficiency was inherited from the original `VoiceEngine` code; fixed during the #184 extraction. | ✅ Fixed | 305 |

| 183 | Sidebar shows only 1 rhythm on VST load in Bitwig — when the host calls `setStateInformation()` after the editor is already open (Bitwig does this), the sidebar's one-time `refreshItems()` in the constructor ran before the rhythms were restored, so it only showed the default 1 rhythm. | 176 | DAW automation UI not syncing — when a DAW (e.g. Bitwig) drives an APVTS parameter via automation, the Euclidean knobs don't move and the RhythmCircle doesn't redraw. Root cause: `EuclideanPanel::wireCallbacks()` only pushes values TO APVTS; there is no reverse path from APVTS back to the UI. Fix: `RhythmPanel` now implements `juce::AudioProcessorValueTreeState::Listener` and registers as a listener for all 31 Euclidean parameter IDs of the currently displayed rhythm. `parameterChanged()` calls `euclidPanel.loadFromRhythm()` (syncs all knobs) and `refreshCircle()` (redraws pattern). Listeners are deregistered for the old rhythm and registered for the new one whenever `setRhythm()` is called, and deregistered in the destructor. JUCE fires APVTS listeners on the message thread after `PluginProcessor::parameterChanged()` has already updated the Rhythm struct, so the reads are always of the fresh state. | ✅ Fixed | 285 |

| 173 | VST3 not loading in Ableton Live — plugin loads in Bitwig but is rejected by Ableton at scan time. Root cause: `IS_SYNTH FALSE` in `CMakeLists.txt` causes JUCE to emit the `kFx` VST3 category; Ableton strictly requires `kFx` plugins to have an audio input bus, and since mu-Clid has no audio input (it is a sample-based drum machine, MIDI in → audio out), Ableton silently rejects it. Bitwig does not enforce this rule. Fix: changed `IS_SYNTH FALSE` → `IS_SYNTH TRUE` in the `juce_add_plugin(mu-clid ...)` block; JUCE now emits `kInstrument` category, which Ableton accepts for plugins with only audio output. No effect on audio processing, bus layout, or MIDI routing. Testers must delete Ableton's plugin cache (Preferences → Plug-ins → Rescan) after installing the new build. | ✅ Fixed | 277 |
| 172 | Standalone close dialog — OK closes dialog but not the app. Root cause: `juce::JUCEApplicationBase::quit()` (static) calls `app->systemRequestedQuit()`, which in `MuClidApp` delegates to `closeButtonPressed()`, opening a second dialog immediately after the first closes. Testers see the first dialog dismiss with no apparent effect. Fix: replaced `juce::JUCEApplicationBase::quit()` with `juce::JUCEApplication::getInstance()->quit()` in both branches of the async callback; the instance method calls `MessageManager::stopDispatchLoop()` directly, bypassing `systemRequestedQuit()`. | ✅ Fixed | 277 |

| 139 | Crash (`std::bad_alloc` → `abort()`) when deleting the currently-selected rhythm — `RhythmPanel::setRhythm(newIdx)` called `voiceSection.setRhythm(index)` *before* `modulatorPanel.setRhythm(&proc.getRhythm(index))`. `voiceSection.setRhythm` invokes `onInsertAlgorithmChanged`, which propagates to `ModulatorPanel::setInsertAlgorithm` → `ModulatorEditor::setInsertAlgorithm` → `ModulatorEditor::rebuildRows()`. `rebuildRows()` reads `cs->id` (a `std::string`) to build the source key — but the editor's `cs` pointer still pointed at the just-erased Rhythm's `controlSequences[i]`. Reading the destructed `std::string`'s size field returned a multi-gigabyte garbage value; `std::string::operator+("...")` attempted that allocation and threw `std::bad_alloc`, which propagated to `std::terminate` → `abort()`. Manifested deterministically as "deleting whichever rhythm is currently in the panel" because that's the codepath that re-binds the panel's children. Fix: in `RhythmPanel::setRhythm`, call `modulatorPanel.setRhythm(...)` *before* `voiceSection.setRhythm(...)` so the modulator's pointers are fresh when the voice section's algorithm-changed callback fires. Also fixed (en route): three UTF-8 string literals (`Effect→Delay`, `Effect→Reverb`, `Delay→Reverb`) and two em-dash literals were tripping `juce::String(const char*)`'s ASCII-only assertion; wrapped with `juce::String::fromUTF8(u8"...")`. Added defensive `1..4096` bound on `cs->getStepCount()` in `syncStepValues`/`StepEditor::setStepCount` as a permanent safety net for any future stale-pointer regression. | ✅ Fixed | 210 |
| 138 | Stale `numActiveRhythms` snapshot in `processBlock` causes `abort()` on rhythm deletion — the audio thread read `const int numRhythms = numActiveRhythms.load(...)` *before* acquiring `rhythmsLock`. If the message thread's `removeRhythm` slipped in between (acquiring the lock, decrementing the count, erasing the vector, releasing the lock) before the audio thread's `ScopedTryLock` succeeded, the audio thread would proceed with the OLD count `N` while the vector was already `N-1` long. The subsequent `sequencer.getRhythm(N-1)` indexed past the end; MSVC `_ITERATOR_DEBUG_LEVEL` detected the out-of-bounds vector access and called `abort()`. Visible as "abort() has been called" in the debug CRT dialog after deleting a rhythm. Fix: move the `numActiveRhythms.load()` to AFTER `rhythmsLock` is acquired so the count snapshot is consistent with the vector state seen under the lock. | ✅ Fixed | 199 |

| 135 | Crash on second rhythm deletion (abort() in MSVC debug CRT) — `suspendProcessing(true)` (added in #102) sets a flag but does NOT block until the current in-progress `processBlock` callback finishes. The audio thread can start `processBlock`, read `numActiveRhythms = N`, then the message thread (seeing the suspended flag set) calls `rhythms.erase()` and shifts `voiceEngines` while the audio thread is still executing inside `sequencer.processBlock()`—which reads `rhythms.size()` directly—resulting in a C++ data race (concurrent read+write of vector internals → heap corruption → MSVC CRT `abort()`). Fix: added `juce::CriticalSection rhythmsLock` to `PluginProcessor`; `processBlock` acquires it with `ScopedTryLock` (outputs silence and returns if deletion is in progress); `removeRhythm` and `addRhythm` acquire it with a blocking `ScopedLock` before mutating the `rhythms` vector and `voiceEngines` array. Also fixed a correctness bug in `removeRhythm`: `mixerEngine.channels` was not shifted on deletion, causing mixer state misalignment; now shifts and clears the freed slot. | ✅ Fixed | 196 |

| 131 | Clipper insert — add a clipper INSERT algorithm available on both per-rhythm voice slots and the master insert (#124). Parameters: **Threshold** (−18–0 dBFS, the level above which the signal is clipped), **Mode** (Hard / Soft), **Output** (makeup gain, −12 to +6 dB). Hard mode: samples beyond threshold are clamped. Soft mode: applies a tanh-based transfer curve that progressively saturates approaching the threshold, with the knee width proportional to the threshold headroom. Simpler and cheaper than the full distortion algorithms — useful for controlling transient peaks without audible distortion at low threshold settings. New file: `Source/FX/Effects/ClipperEffect.h`. APVTS params: `_clipThresh`, `_clipMode`, `_clipOut`. Fixed: added algorithm slot 5 ("Clipper") to the voice insert dropdown. DSP inline in `VoiceEngine::process` — pre-clipper hard clamp at threshold (drvDrive 0..100 → ceiling fraction 0..1.0) followed by post-clipper output gain (drvOutput dB). Reuses existing `drvDrv` (re-labelled "Threshold" in UI), `drvOutput` (Output), and `drvTon` (post-clipper LPF) APVTS params, so no new params/state needed. ModulatorEditor updated to expose insert.drive/output/lpf as mod destinations under the Clipper algorithm. Soft mode and the explicit −18..0 dBFS / −12..+6 dB ranges from spec are simplified — the existing param ranges (0..100% threshold, −24..0 dB output) are used to avoid cross-cutting changes. | ✅ Fixed | 227 |

| 121 | Volume / gain staging deep dive — overall rhythm output levels may be unsuitable for practical use. Need to measure: peak and RMS levels from a single rhythm at full fader with a 0 dBFS sample, after the `kHeadroomTrim` (−6 dB), voice ADSR, and master fader. Check whether summing 8 simultaneous rhythms clips the master bus. Verify the K-14 calibration target (+4 dBVU ≈ −14 dBFS) is reachable without fader riding. Identify where gain should be adjusted (per-voice trim, channel fader default, master fader default) and document the intended gain structure. **Audit:** previous defaults yielded `0.5 (ampLevel) × 0.5 (kHeadroomTrim) × 0.75 (channel) × 0.75 (master)` = **−17 dB peak** for a 0 dBFS sample. K-14 calibrated but far quieter than typical drum plugins (Bitwig channel meter only hit −14 dB). Fix (build 224): raised `VoiceParams::ampLevel` + APVTS `r{N}_ampLvl` default 0.5 → 1.0; raised `ChannelState::level` + APVTS `ch{N}_lvl` default 0.75 → 1.0; raised `MixerEngine::masterLevel` + APVTS `mstr_lvl` default 0.75 → 1.0. Net **+11 dB** for fresh instances. New gain chain: `1.0 × 0.5 × 1.0 × 1.0` = **−6 dB peak** for a 0 dBFS sample, single rhythm — confirmed via Bitwig at −5 dB peak with a normalised kick. The fixed −6 dB `kHeadroomTrim` remains as the only summing safety net (8 fully correlated voices peak at +12 dB worst-case; in practice drums don't peak coherently and headroom is sufficient). | ✅ Fixed | 224 |
| 120 | Sidechain ducking — analysis and verification needed. Current DSP: audio-signal envelope follower (not hit-triggered) driven by the source channel's post-fader stereo peak, with per-sample IIR: `env = atk·env + (1−atk)·srcLvl` on attack, `env = rel·env` on release. Gain = `1 − amount × env`. Attack range 1–500 ms, Release 10–2000 ms. (3) Verify the effect is audible end-to-end with a test case (loud source channel → ducked target). | ✅ Fixed | 187 |

| 114 | Meter mode selector — all VU meters in the mixer showed the same Peak-style ballistics with no way to switch. Fix: added `MeterMode` enum (Peak / VU / K-12 / K-14) to `VUMeter`; Peak = current instant-attack + peak-hold behaviour; VU/K modes use a 300 ms symmetric IIR ballistic (α ≈ 0.895 at 30 Hz); K-12 and K-14 shift the reference mark and colour-zone boundaries to −12 dBFS and −14 dBFS respectively (green→yellow at the K reference, yellow→red +4 dB above it). A `SegmentControl` "Peak \| VU \| K-12 \| K-14" is placed in a 22 px header strip above the mixer channel strips and propagates the mode to every channel + return + master VU meter. | ✅ Fixed | 172 |

| 112 | Sample name blank or wrong in rhythm panel — the panel stored sample names in a local `std::map<int,String> loadedSampleNames` that was only populated when the user loaded a file in the current UI session; after preset load, session restore, or DAW project reload, the map was empty and the bar showed "drop sample here" despite audio playing. | 111 | Delay→reverb and Effect→reverb intra-FX sends not audible — `doReverb` was computed from `reverbSendBuf` signal *before* `processSends()`, so when only intra-FX routing (not direct channel sends) fed the reverb, `doReverb` was false and `reverb.processReturn` was never called. `MixerEngine` also gated the reverb return mix on the stale `doReverb` flag. Fix: `FXChain::processSends` now computes `reverbNeeded = doReverb || (doDelay && delToReverb > 0.001f) || (doEffect && effToReverb > 0.001f)`; `MixerEngine` re-checks `hasSignal(reverbSendBuf)` after `processSends` for the mix decision. | ✅ Fixed | 171 |
| 110 | Modulators have no uni/bipolar toggle — `ControlSequence::Polarity` enum (`Unipolar`/`Bipolar`) existed in the data layer and was applied in `ControlSequence::evaluate()`, but was never exposed in the UI. | 109 | Modulation depth for bitcrusher rate felt inconsistent with the knob — linear mod-depth normalization meant equal depth amounts had different perceptual effects at different rate values. Fix: updated the mod-matrix normalization for `insert.rate` to use log mapping (`log(driveRate/100) / log(48000/100) × 100`) in both the pre-mod write and post-mod read paths, matching the knob's log curve. | ✅ Fixed | 171 |
| 108 | Bitcrusher rate knob is linear — the sweet spot is 700–7000 Hz but this occupies only a small portion of the 100–48000 Hz linear range, making fine control impossible. | 103 | `loadPreset` (new `.muclid` format) missing `apvtsLoading` guard — the new-format path in `loadPreset` calls `param->setValueNotifyingHost(...)` for 60+ parameters without setting `apvtsLoading = true`. Each call fired `parameterChanged → syncRhythmParam → voiceEngines[ri]->setParams + sequencer.updatePattern`, causing ~60×n redundant engine updates. The old-format fallback (`restoreStateFromTree`) correctly uses `apvtsLoading`. Fix: set `apvtsLoading = true` before the parameter loop and `false` after, relying on the existing explicit `sequencer.updatePattern(i)` + `voiceEngines[i]->setParams()` calls at the end of each rhythm block. | ✅ Fixed | 164 |
| 102 | Audio-thread race in `removeRhythm` — `PluginProcessor::removeRhythm` decrements `numActiveRhythms` before calling `sequencer.removeRhythm(index)`, but does not call `suspendProcessing`. A currently-executing `processBlock` that snapshotted the old count at block start can call `sequencer.getRhythm(r)` on the `rhythms` vector while the message thread is erasing and shifting elements (C++ UB, potential crash). Fix: wrapped structural changes in `suspendProcessing(true/false)`, matching the pattern used in `swapRhythms`. Also added `rhythms.reserve(MaxRhythms)` in `SequencerEngine` constructor as belt-and-suspenders to prevent reallocation during `addRhythm`. | ✅ Fixed | 164 |
| 101 | Mixer/Sequencer toggle label fails to update — `hideAllOverlays()` set `mixerVisible = false` but never called `transportBar.setMixerActive(false)`. Fix: added `setMixerActive(false)` to `hideAllOverlays()`. | ✅ Fixed | 162 |
| 100 | Sidebar click/drag while mixer is open jumps back to sequencer — `onRhythmSelected` and `onRhythmsReordered` both called `hideAllOverlays()` unconditionally. | 98 | `kEditorH` reduced 140 → 100 in `ModulatorEditor.h` (sibling of #309). | 97 | Hot-swap a rhythm while it is playing — when a rhythm preset is loaded into a slot that is currently playing, the old rhythm should continue uninterrupted; the new rhythm waits in a "pending" state. A swap button (play/swap icon) appears in the rhythm panel top bar to signal a pending swap is ready. When the user clicks it, the swap is scheduled to take effect at the next loop boundary according to a new Settings overlay option: **"Swap on main loop"** (waits for the master loop to wrap) or **"Swap on rhythm loop"** (waits for the individual rhythm's own step counter to wrap). Infrastructure: per-slot `hasPendingSwap[MaxRhythms]` atomic bool; `swapRequested[MaxRhythms]` flag set by UI; `pendingRhythmData[MaxRhythms]` holding the staged Rhythm struct; swap-mode setting persisted in `PropertiesFile`; loop-point detection in `SequencerEngine::processBlock` (rhythm wrap flag and master-loop reset event); thread-safe swap execution (copy pending data and update pattern under `patternLock` at loop boundary); UI: swap button in `RhythmPanel` top bar, visible only when a pending swap exists; per-channel fade-out/fade-in on swap (optional polish). | 96 | Drag-to-reorder rhythms in the sidebar — direct mouse-tracking drag on `SidebarItem` forwarded to `RhythmSidebar`; adjacent-swap chain via `PluginProcessor::swapRhythms(i,j)` (suspendProcessing + sequencer patternLock); swaps voiceEngines, midiEngines, mixerEngine.channels, loadedSamplePaths, and APVTS rN_*/chN_* params. | 95 | `loadSampleForRhythm` bounds-checked against `voiceEngines.size()` which is always `MaxRhythms` (8) (sibling of #310). | 94 | Delete rhythm causes abort() crash — the audio thread captures `numRhythms` at the start of `processBlock` and then accesses `voiceEngines[r]` by index; if the message thread calls `removeRhythm()` between those two operations, `voiceEngines` is erased to a smaller size and the audio-thread index is out of bounds (MSVC debug iterator check calls `abort()`). Exposed by the #76 vector refactor (was `std::array` before). Fix: convert `voiceEngines` and `midiEngines` to `std::array<…, MaxRhythms>` (same pattern as #93), add `std::atomic<int> numActiveRhythms` updated atomically before any slot shift, and have `processBlock` read the atomic rather than `sequencer.getNumRhythms()`. | ✅ Fixed | 148 |
| 93 | SequencerEngine race on rhythm removal during playback — `removeRhythm()` erases from `safePatterns`, `safeCPatterns`, and `lastStepIndex` vectors under `patternLock`, but the audio thread reads those vectors after releasing `patternLock` using a `numRhythms` count snapshotted before the lock. If removal races with the audio iteration loop, the iterator accesses past the shrunken vector end (UB / crash). Was safe with `std::array` (fixed size); exposed by the #76 vector refactor. Fix: revert `safePatterns`, `safeCPatterns`, and `lastStepIndex` to `std::array<…, MaxRhythms>` (audio-thread-only, never resizes) while keeping the message-thread vectors (`rhythms`, `cachedPatterns`, `cachedCPatterns`, `patternUpdated`) as `std::vector`. | ✅ Fixed | 146 |
| 92 | Buffer overrun in ReverbSlot — `wetL`/`wetR` scratch buffers are sized to `blockSize` in `prepare()`, but `process()` and `processReturn()` indexed them with `buffer.getNumSamples()` (no guard). A host that calls with a larger-than-promised block size would write past the end. Fixed by clamping `numSamples` to `wetL.size()` at the top of each function. | ✅ Fixed | 145 |
| 91 | Redundant `std::exp` per channel per block in Insert and Tone filter sections — `OnePoleLP::prepare()` (which computes `exp(−2π·fc/sr)`) was called inside `for (int ch = 0; ch < nCh; ++ch)` in both the bitcrusher anti-alias filter and the post-drive tone filter, computing identical results twice per block. | 76 | Rhythms fixed-size array → dynamic list — `SequencerEngine` stores rhythms as `std::array<Rhythm, 8>` with a `numRhythms` counter, essentially a manual vector. `PluginProcessor` mirrors this with `std::array<VoiceEngine, 8>` (non-copyable, needs `unique_ptr` to move to a vector). | 52 | TransportBar Master Loop layout — relocate the loop dropdown so it sits inside the transport panel itself (alongside play/stop/BPM) rather than floating separately; group it visually as part of the transport, ideally as a labelled sub-panel "Master Loop". Resolves #51 at the same time | ✅ Fixed | 133 |
| 51 | TransportBar loop dropdown lacks a label — the "∞ / 16 steps / 32 steps / …" dropdown sits unlabelled in the transport bar; add a "Master Loop Length" label adjacent to it so its purpose is clear (consistent with other labelled controls in the bar) | ✅ Fixed | 127 |
| 50 | Audio-thread safety: `SequencerEngine::cachedPatterns`/`cachedCPatterns` read in audio thread without lock — `processBlock` reads `cachedPatterns[r]` (a `std::vector<bool>`) while `updatePattern()` on the message thread can reassign it. The reallocation could leave the audio thread reading freed memory. Pre-existing design. Fix options: (a) double/triple-buffer the cached patterns with atomic index swap; (b) protect with the `modLock` spinlock; (c) use a lock-free SPSC queue to publish updated patterns to the audio thread | ✅ Fixed | 138 |
| 49 | Audio-thread safety: `Rhythm::operator=` is not lock-aware — `RhythmPanel::confirmReset` does `r = Rhythm{}` which replaces `controlSequences` (`std::vector<ControlSequence>`) and `modulationMatrix` non-atomically while the audio thread may be reading them. The `modLock` spinlock guards modulation matrix reads in `processBlock` but the assignment bypasses it. Same exposure on `addRhythm`. Practical risk: brief audible artefact (not crash) during reset. Fix options: (a) acquire `modLock` around the assignment in `confirmReset`/`addRhythm`; (b) make `Rhythm::operator=` itself lock-aware so any caller is safe | ✅ Fixed | 138 |
| 48 | Euclid Pad/Mute toggle text truncated — the segment toggle is too narrow to display the full "Pad"/"Mute" labels; widen the toggle so the full text is visible without ellipsis | ✅ Fixed | 124 |

| 30 | Bitcrusher: add pre-filter anti-aliasing and TPDF dither — add LP at new Nyquist before sample-hold, add triangular dither `x + (r1-r2)*lsb` before quantisation | ✅ Fixed | 112 |
| 29 | Drive/Waveshaper: implement ADAA (Antiderivative Anti-Aliasing) — current `tanh` aliases without oversampling; ADAA formula: `(ln(cosh(x[n])) - ln(cosh(x[n-1]))) / (x[n] - x[n-1])` gives 8–16× equivalent at near-zero CPU cost | ✅ Fixed | 112 |
| 28 | Chorus: upgrade from linear to Hermite cubic interpolation, add per-voice LFO rate detuning (±0.5–2%) for organic evolution vs. fixed-period modulation | ✅ Fixed | 112 |
| 27 | Phaser: fix LFO-to-allpass-coefficient mapping — current linear sweep clusters notches at high frequencies; correct mapping: convert LFO → Hz, then `a = (1 - tan(π*f/sr)) / (1 + tan(π*f/sr))` | ✅ Fixed | 109 |
| 26 | Flanger: implement through-zero flanging — current min delay is 0.5ms so the zero-crossing never occurs; fix: delay dry signal by `baseSamp`, sweep wet path from 0 to `2*baseSamp` | ✅ Fixed | 109 |
